  <script>
   window.IcreateElementChangeListener= function (selector, callback) {
    const initializedNodes = new Set([]);

    document.querySelectorAll(selector).forEach((node) => {
        callback(node);
        initializedNodes.add(node);
    });

    const mutationObserver = new MutationObserver(() => {
        const nodes = document.querySelectorAll(selector);
        nodes.forEach((node) => {
            if (!initializedNodes.has(node)) {
                callback(node);
                initializedNodes.add(node);
            }
        });
    });

    mutationObserver.observe(document.body, {
        childList: true,
        subtree: true,
    });
}

 window.setCookie__ = function (cname,cvalue,exdays) {
    var d = new Date();
    d.setTime(d.getTime() + (exdays * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000));
    var expires = "expires="+d.toUTCString();
   
    document.cookie = cname + "=" + cvalue + ";" + expires +";path=/"; ;
}

window.getCookie= function (cname) {
    var name = cname + "=";
    var decodedCookie = decodeURIComponent(document.cookie);
    var ca = decodedCookie.split(';');
    for(var i = 0; i < ca.length; i++) {
        var c = ca[i];
        while (c.charAt(0) == ' ') {
            c = c.substring(1);
        }
        if (c.indexOf(name) == 0) {
            return c.substring(name.length, c.length);
        }
    }
    return "";

"order": 9}, {"amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "display": true, "new_amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "order": 10}],                   </script>
                  <div class="body-description">
                   <div class="widget__brief">
                    <p>
                     By Hannah Thomasy
                    </p>
                    <p>
                     On its own, a single sea cucumber may not be very impressive. But get enough of these floppy, faceless creatures together, and they—or, more specifically, their poop—can physically and biochemically reshape a coral reef habitat.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <div class="content-container">
                   </div>
                   <div class="js-appear-on-expand">
                    <template>
                     &lt;p&gt;In a recently published &lt;a href="https://link.springer.com/article/10.1007/s00338-021-02057-2" target="_blank"&gt;study&lt;/a&gt;, an Australian research team used drone surveys, satellite imagery, and observations of individual sea cucumbers to estimate how much poop the sea cucumbers of Heron Island Reef produced per year. Heron Island Reef is part of the southern Great Barrier Reef system off the coast of Queensland, Australia.&lt;/p&gt;
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-1" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/sea-cucumbers-coral-reefs" data-id="1" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651162193" data-published-at="1616358975" id="rebelltitem1">
                      &lt;p&gt;Historically, one of the major problems scientists have faced when trying to assess the importance of sea cucumbers (and their excrement) in the reef ecosystem is the difficulty in assessing just how many sea cucumbers there are in a given area, said &lt;a href="https://researchers.mq.edu.au/en/persons/jane-williamson" target="_blank"&gt;Jane Williamson&lt;/a&gt;, the study's lead author and head of the Marine Ecology Group at Macquarie University.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Previous research used footage from boats or information collected by divers to estimate sea cucumber numbers, said Williamson. But boats stir up the water, making it difficult to see the animals, and divers can collect information over only relatively small areas, resulting in a high degree of uncertainty when their observations were used to extrapolate the population of the entire reef.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;So Williamson and her team, which included coral reef geomorphologist &lt;a href="https://research.jcu.edu.au/portfolio/stephanie.duce/" target="_blank"&gt;Stephanie Duce&lt;/a&gt;, remote sensing expert &lt;a href="https://research.jcu.edu.au/portfolio/karen.joyce/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;Karen Joyce&lt;/a&gt;, and marine ecologist &lt;a href="https://www.newcastle.edu.au/profile/vincent-raoult" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;Vincent Raoult&lt;/a&gt;, wanted to try a different method. Using images captured by drones, the team surveyed sea cucumbers over tens of thousands of square meters in two different geomorphic zones (the inner and the outer reef flats). Researchers then used satellite imagery to determine the area of each of these geomorphic zones to extrapolate the number of sea cucumbers present on the entire reef. These methods indicated that there were more than 3 million sea cucumbers on the reef flats surrounding Heron Island Reef.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The team also collected dozens of individual sea cucumbers to observe their bioturbation rates—that is, how much each sea cucumber pooped in a given day. On average, each sea cucumber produced about 38 grams of poop in 24 hours. Using this information, along with their estimates of the reef's sea cucumber population, researchers determined that on a single reef, sea cucumbers produced more than 64,000 metric tons of poop per year—more than the weight of five Eiffel Towers.&lt;/p&gt;
                     </div>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-2" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/sea-cucumbers-coral-reefs" data-id="2" data-is-image="True" data-post-id="2651162193" data-published-at="1616358975" id="rebelltitem2">
                      &lt;img lazy-loadable="true" data-runner-src="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTg1NzY2OC9vcmlnaW4ucG5nIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTYyNDg1ODk0Mn0.sdUl46Tt_7YiBC-xToq2HD9Yt_Aosogf2NY24bmZrgE/img.png?width=980" id="d1257" class="rm-shortcode" data-rm-shortcode-id="b9eec7b4cd791bda32d25c244c634ee7" data-rm-shortcode-name="rebelmouse-image"   data-width="1252" data-height="882" /&gt;
                      <small class="image-media media-photo-credit">
                      </small>
                      <p>
                       By measuring how much individual sea cucumbers pooped per day and estimating the number of sea cucumbers on the reef using drones and satellite images, researchers determined how much poop sea cucumbers contributed to the Heron Island Reef. Credit: Associate Professor Jane Williamson et al., 2021, Macquarie University; Dr. Stephanie Duce, James Cook University; Dr. Karen Joyce, James Cook University; and Dr. Vincent Raoult, University of Newcastle.
                       <a href="https://doi.org/10.1007/s00338-021-02057-2" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
                        https://doi.org/10.1007/s00338-021-02057-2
                       </a>
                      </p>
                     </div>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="the-importance-of-excrement" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/sea-cucumbers-coral-reefs" data-id="4" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651162193" data-published-at="1616359091" id="rebelltitem4">
                      <h3 data-role="headline">
                       The Importance of Excrement
                      </h3>
                      &lt;p&gt;Scientists think that all of that poop plays an important role in ecosystem health as well as in the biogeochemical cycles of the reef.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"Sea cucumbers can be considered like a long sausage, almost," said Williamson. "Sediment goes in and sediment comes out.… By eating the sediment and then pooping it out again, they're actually aerating the sediment, which makes the sediment a healthier place for other animals to live, like small crabs or &lt;a href="https://ucmp.berkeley.edu/annelida/polyintro.html" target="_blank"&gt;polychaetes&lt;/a&gt;, which are worms, or small mollusks that live inside the sediment in the surface layer."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Sea cucumbers are also involved in the nitrogen cycles of the reef ecosystem. As sea cucumbers eat and excrete sediment, "they're releasing nitrogen that's trapped in between the sediments," said Williamson. "So this is really important because nitrogen in particular is a limiting nutrient on coral reefs.… The corals need nitrogen, and the algae need nitrogen, everything sort of locks it up really quickly when it's available, so the sea cucumbers are doing them a big favor in terms of the growth rate of these organisms."&lt;/p&gt;
                     </div>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-3" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/sea-cucumbers-coral-reefs" data-id="3" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651162193" data-published-at="1616358975" id="rebelltitem3">
                      &lt;iframe src="https://giphy.com/embed/B1wejiJEnNt7S6gMWC" width="480" height="270" frameBorder="0" class="giphy-embed" allowFullScreen&gt;&lt;/iframe&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href="https://giphy.com/gifs/natgeowild-poop-nat-geo-wild-national-geographic-B1wejiJEnNt7S6gMWC"&gt;via GIPHY&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Sea cucumbers could even help protect coral reefs against one of the harmful side effects of climate change: ocean acidification. "The oceans are becoming more acidic, which means that the calcium carbonate which makes the skeletons of the corals and things is less available and in some cases is actually dissolving off the corals." In addition to releasing nitrogen, sea cucumbers also increase the availability of calcium carbonate as they eat their way through the sediment, said Williamson. "So for the sea cucumbers to release more calcium carbonate that's been trapped in the sediments into the environment that the corals and other animals can use is super important."&lt;br&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"These little sausages are playing a really key role that people just don't think about," said Williamson.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href="https://www.scu.edu.au/about/contacts/staff-directory/staff/28260.php" target="_blank"&gt;Steven Purcell&lt;/a&gt;, a marine scientist at Southern Cross University in Lismore, Australia, who was not associated with the study, said that more than 70 countries harvest sea cucumbers. Because these animals are of great ecological value, it's important to keep tabs on their numbers to make sure they're not being overharvested. He noted that drone surveillance techniques like the one used in this paper could also be used to assess populations of other exploited shallow-water reef species, like giant clams.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;This story originally appeared in &lt;/em&gt;&lt;em&gt;&lt;a href="https://eos.org/articles/sea-cucumbers-the-excremental-heroes-of-coral-reef-ecosystems" target="_blank"&gt;Eos&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/em&gt; &lt;em&gt;and is republished here as part of Covering Climate Now, a global journalism collaboration strengthening coverage of the climate story.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
                     </div>

                 <h2 class="widget__headline h2">
                  <a aria-label="11 Surprising Facts About Trees" class="widget__headline-text custom-post-headline" data-type="text" href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tree-facts-2651160331.html">
                   11 Surprising Facts About Trees
                  </a>
                 </h2>
                 <div class="social-author clearfix">
                  <div class="social-author__avatar image">
                   <div class="cover-all image" style='background-image: url("https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8xODcxNDI4Ni9vcmlnaW4ucG5nIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTY2ODI3MDgxOH0.dfBxicmxbE7_p1-p0AV9PoNawJYfQRb9jBVA5elPEyk/img.png?width=210")'>
                   </div>
                  </div>
                  <a class="social-author__name" data-type="text" href="https://www.ecowatch.com/u/deutschewelle">
                   Deutsche Welle
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="social-date">
                  <span class="social-date__text">
                   7h
                  </span>
                 </div>
                 <a class="widget__section js-load-brick-on-click" href="https://www.ecowatch.com/popular/">
                  Popular
                 </a>
                </div>
                <div class="widget__head">
                 <a aria-label="11 Surprising Facts About Trees" href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tree-facts-2651160331.html">
                  <div aria-label="11 Surprising Facts About Trees" class="widget__image crop-16x9" data-runner-img-hd="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTg1NzI2Ni9vcmlnaW4uanBnIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTYyMjExMDAxOH0.OOSlk_dkJZWww4JdZFXv9r0d6-bK9DlhZ2GmZuLzk2s/img.jpg?width=1245&amp;quality=85&amp;coordinates=0%2C0%2C0%2C0&amp;height=700" data-runner-img-md="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTg1NzI2Ni9vcmlnaW4uanBnIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTYyMjExMDAxOH0.OOSlk_dkJZWww4JdZFXv9r0d6-bK9DlhZ2GmZuLzk2s/img.jpg?width=1245&amp;quality=85&amp;coordinates=0%2C0%2C0%2C0&amp;height=700" data-runner-img-sd="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTg1NzI2Ni9vcmlnaW4uanBnIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTYyMjExMDAxOH0.OOSlk_dkJZWww4JdZFXv9r0d6-bK9DlhZ2GmZuLzk2s/img.jpg?width=980&amp;quality=85" data-runner-style="padding-bottom: 56.25%;" data-type="image" role="img" style="padding-bottom: 56.25%;">
                   <div class="lazyload-placeholder">
                    <div class="runner-spinner">
                     <svg class="runner-spinner-circular" viewbox="25 25 50 50">
                      <circle class="runner-spinner-path" cx="50" cy="50" fill="none" r="20" stroke-miterlimit="10" stroke-width="3">
                      </circle>
                     </svg>
                    </div>
                   </div>
                  </div>
                 </a>
                </div>
                <div class="widget__body clearfix sm-mt-1">
                 <div class="photo-credit">
                  <em>
                   Pexels
                  </em>
                 </div>

                  </script>
                  <div class="body-description">
                   <div class="widget__brief">
                    <p>
                     By Natalie Muller
                    </p>
                    <p>
                     Trees soak up carbon from the atmosphere, provide a home to wildlife and even improve our mental well-being. But did you know they can also "talk" to each other, and send out distress signals when under attack?
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <div class="content-container">
                   </div>
                   <div class="js-appear-on-expand">
                    <template>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="1-60-000-different-species" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tree-facts" data-id="1" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651160331" data-published-at="1616340844" id="rebelltitem1">
                      <h3 data-role="headline">
                       1. ​60,000 Different Species
                      </h3>
                      &lt;p&gt;There are around 3 trillion trees on Earth, according to a global study led by researchers from Yale University. That includes over 60,000 known tree species, more than half of which are endemic — meaning they're found in only one country. Brazil, Colombia and Indonesia are home to the most tree species. The bad news: there are 46% fewer trees today than at the start of human civilization.&lt;/p&gt;
                     </div>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="2-trees-migrate-to-escape-climate-change" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tree-facts" data-id="2" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651160331" data-published-at="1616340844" id="rebelltitem2">
                      <h3 data-role="headline">
                       2. Trees 'Migrate' to Escape Climate Change
                      </h3>
                      &lt;p&gt;Trees clearly can't uproot themselves and move, but their population centers can shift over time in response to climate pressures. A study looking at 86 trees species between 1980 and 2015 in the eastern United States found that 73% moved west, where rainfall is increasing. Others headed to the poles, apparently to escape heat. On average, they moved about 16 kilometers (10 miles) per decade.&lt;/p&gt;
                     </div>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="3-keeping-cities-cool" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tree-facts" data-id="3" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651160331" data-published-at="1616340844" id="rebelltitem3">
                      <h3 data-role="headline">
                       3. Keeping Cities Cool
                      </h3>
                      &lt;p&gt;Trees not only give us shade, they can also mitigate extreme temperatures by transpiring — absorbing the sun's radiation and releasing water into the air through their leaves. Urban areas can become sweltering "heat islands" in summer. But a 2019 study from the US found that tree canopy cover of 40% or more could lower summer temperatures in cities by as much as 5 degrees Celsius.&lt;/p&gt;
                     </div>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="4-sucking-up-pollutants" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tree-facts" data-id="4" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651160331" data-published-at="1616340844" id="rebelltitem4">
                      <h3 data-role="headline">
                       4. Sucking Up Pollutants
                      </h3>
                      &lt;p&gt;Trees draw CO2 from the atmosphere and are therefore crucial in the fight against climate change. They can also use their leaves to filter particulate matter and toxic gases like nitrogen dioxide and sulphur dioxide from the air. A recent UK study found that silver birch, yew and elder trees could reduce particles at rates of 79%, 71% and 70% respectively.&lt;/p&gt;
                     </div>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="5-healing-power" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tree-facts" data-id="5" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651160331" data-published-at="1616340844" id="rebelltitem5">
                      <h3 data-role="headline">
                       5. Healing Power
                      </h3>
                      &lt;p&gt;Trees can reduce our stress levels and help us feel happier and healthier. Several studies have shown that spending time in nature, or even just looking at trees or flowers through a window, can lower blood pressure, boost the immune system, improve sleep, reduce depression and anxiety, and even speed up recovery after surgery.&lt;/p&gt;
                     </div>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="6-trees-talk-to-each-other" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tree-facts" data-id="6" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651160331" data-published-at="1616340844" id="rebelltitem6">
                      <h3 data-role="headline">
                       6. Trees 'Talk' to Each Other
                      </h3>
                      &lt;p&gt;Forests have their own communication systems — almost like an underground internet —that allows trees to swap nutrients and send warnings about drought or disease. They interact via networks of soil fungi, known as mycorrhizal networks. Research by ecologist Suzanne Simard has shown that paper birch (pictured) and fir trees use this system to send water, carbon and nutrients back and forth.&lt;/p&gt;
                     </div>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="7-sending-signals-in-the-air" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tree-facts" data-id="7" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651160331" data-published-at="1616340844" id="rebelltitem7">
                      <h3 data-role="headline">
                       7. Sending Signals in the Air
                      </h3>
                      &lt;p&gt;Trees can't flee if their leaves are being devoured by a hungry herbivore. But what they can do is release chemicals — volatile organic compounds — into the air to warn nearby members of the same species there's a threat in the area. Studies show that other trees respond by boosting their own production of anti-herbivore toxins, which, in the case of acacias (pictured), makes their leaves bitter.&lt;/p&gt;
                     </div>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="8-call-for-backup" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tree-facts" data-id="8" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651160331" data-published-at="1616340844" id="rebelltitem8">
                      <h3 data-role="headline">
                       8. Call for Backup
                      </h3>
                      &lt;p&gt;When besieged by bugs or parasites, some species, including apple trees, and tomato, cucumber and lima bean plants, release compounds into the air to alert the attackers' predator. Most often, these predators are insects. But a European study showed that trees infested with caterpillars also put out chemical signals to attract caterpillar-eating birds, such as the great tit (pictured).&lt;/p&gt;
                     </div>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="9-methuselah-has-lived-through-a-lot" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tree-facts" data-id="9" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651160331" data-published-at="1616340844" id="rebelltitem9">
                      <h3 data-role="headline">
                       9. Methuselah Has Lived Through a Lot
                      </h3>
                      &lt;p&gt;Trees are the oldest living organisms on Earth. One individual can survive hundreds, even thousands of years. According to the OldList, an officially dated record of ancient trees, the oldest known living individual is a bristlecone pine in California's White Mountains. Named Methuselah, it's around 4,850 years old. Its exact location is kept a secret to protect it from vandals.&lt;/p&gt;
                     </div>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="10-hyperion-the-giant" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tree-facts" data-id="10" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651160331" data-published-at="1616340844" id="rebelltitem10">
                      <h3 data-role="headline">
                       10. Hyperion, the Giant
                      </h3>
                      &lt;p&gt;A photograph can't really do justice to the world's tallest trees: redwoods. The tallest known living specimen is a coast redwood called Hyperion measuring 115.85 meters (380 feet) — more than Big Ben or the Statue of Liberty. The giant, discovered in 2006 in California, is believed to be several hundred years old.&lt;/p&gt;
                     </div>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="11-other-record-breakers" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tree-facts" data-id="11" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651160331" data-published-at="1616340844" id="rebelltitem11">
                      <h3 data-role="headline">
                       11. Other Record Breakers
                      </h3>
                      &lt;p&gt;California is also home to a giant sequoia named General Sherman, thought to be the biggest living tree in terms of volume. It stretches to a height of 83.8 meters and is 7.7 meters in diameter. The title of the world's widest tree goes to the Arbol del Tule (pictured), a Montezuma cypress in the Mexican state of Oaxaca. It has a diameter of 11.6 meters and a circumference of 42 meters.​&lt;/p&gt;
                     </div>
                     &lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Reposted with permission from &lt;/em&gt;&lt;em&gt;&lt;a href="https://www.dw.com/en/11-surprising-facts-about-trees/g-54203497" target="_blank"&gt;Deutsche Welle&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;a href="https://www.facebook.com/sharer/sharer.php?u=https%3A%2F%2Fp.dw.com%2Fp%2F3fQnx%3Fmaca%3Den-Facebook-sharing" target="_blank"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;

                     </div>

            <div class="widget tag-indoor-gardening tag-indoor-plants tag-gardening tag-houseplants tag-plants post-section--reviews" data-category="Reviews" elid="2651139034">
             <article class="clearfix page-article sm-mb-1 quality-MD post-2651139034" data-is-frozen="false" elid="2651139034">
              <div class="row px10">
               <div class="col sm-mb-1" id="col-center" style="width:100.0%;">
                <div class="widget__body clearfix sm-mt-1">
                 <div class="post-tags-primary">
                  <a class="post-tags-primary-link" href="/tag/plants">
                   plants
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <h2 class="widget__headline h2">
                  <a aria-label="The Best Houseplants for Your Indoor Garden" class="widget__headline-text custom-post-headline" data-type="text" href="https://www.ecowatch.com/best-houseplants-for-indoor-gardens-2651139034.html">
                   The Best Houseplants for Your Indoor Garden
                  </a>
                 </h2>
                 <div class="social-author clearfix">

                  <div class="body-description">
                   <div class="widget__brief">
                    <p>
                     Nurturing plant life can be a highly fulfilling activity, no matter where you choose to garden. Through
                     <a data-linked-post="2650995230" href="https://www.ecowatch.com/grow-lights-for-indoor-plants-2650995230.html" target="_blank">
                      indoor gardening
                     </a>
                     , you can maintain more delicate or climate-sensitive plants, including succulents and
                     <a data-linked-post="2651105600" href="https://www.ecowatch.com/best-indoor-herb-gardens-2651105600.html" target="_blank">
                      herbs
                     </a>
                     , while also filling your home with vivacious greenery.
                     <br/>
                    </p>
                    <p>
                     Whether you're just getting started with indoor gardening or you're an old pro, it's helpful to know some of the best indoor houseplants. In this article, you'll find a guide to some of the top flora for indoor gardening enthusiasts.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <div class="content-container">
                   </div>
                   <div class="js-appear-on-expand">
                    <template>
                     &lt;h2&gt;How to Choose the Best Houseplants&lt;/h2&gt;&lt;p&gt;When it comes to selecting the right houseplants, there are a number of factors you'll want to keep in mind. Here are some of the considerations we made in creating our list.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul class="ee-ul"&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Light conditions.&lt;/strong&gt; It's important to know whether a plant needs bright light, medium light, indirect light, or low light to flourish. Can your plant thrive with indirect sunlight or does it need a lot of direct sunlight? Will you need to invest in a particular kind of &lt;a href="https://extension.missouri.edu/publications/g6515" target="_blank"&gt;indoor grow light&lt;/a&gt;?&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;The size of the plant.&lt;/strong&gt; Indoor plants range from tiny little things that you can keep on your desk, to more substantial plants that need to be potted on the floor. Naturally, in selecting indoor houseplants, you'll want to think about the space available to you.&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Level of care.&lt;/strong&gt; Some plants need a lot of TLC. Others can essentially be left on their own most of the time. Think about the level of involvement you wish to have in your indoor plant's life and development.&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Pet-friendliness. &lt;/strong&gt;Sometimes, houseplants and pets don't mix. Be sure you don't invest in flora that could tempt your dog or cat into nibbling, or that could actually be toxic if ingested.&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Functionality.&lt;/strong&gt; Some people want indoor houseplants just to look pretty. That's totally fine! Others actually want their houseplants to help clean the air inside their home. If that's what you're looking for, you'll want to be diligent in selecting the right species.&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;The style of plant. &lt;/strong&gt;Do you prefer a potted plant? A hanging basket? A blooming, vertical, or cascade style? Take some time to think about your aesthetic preferences before you invest in houseplants of any kind.&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;With these criteria in mind, we're now ready to take a closer look at the best houseplants to buy for your indoor garden.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h2&gt;The Best Indoor Plants&lt;/h2&gt;&lt;p&gt;Here are our picks for the 12 best indoor plants.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Each product featured here has been independently selected by the writer. If you make a purchase using the links included, we may earn commission.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

                      <h3 data-role="headline">
                       <a href="https://www.amazon.com/Golden-Devils-Ivy-Pothos-Epipremnum/dp/B0076ZJ21K/" target="_blank">
                        Pothos
                       </a>
                      </h3>
                      &lt;img type="lazy-image" data-runner-src="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTg1MDM1NS9vcmlnaW4uanBnIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTYzMDIwMDA4MH0.pAeO0iLWCvi9TGzh_qyMc2vJMbQutGARR6cmViz2Np8/img.jpg?width=980" id="5dacd" class="rm-shortcode" data-rm-shortcode-id="a2b1bc6a1b92af4fe0d8641081764627" data-rm-shortcode-name="rebelmouse-image" alt="Pothos"  data-width="400" data-height="400" /&gt;

                      &lt;p&gt;The &lt;a href="https://www.amazon.com/Golden-Devils-Ivy-Pothos-Epipremnum/dp/B0076ZJ21K/" target="_blank"&gt;pothos&lt;/a&gt; is sometimes known as the "cubicle plant," a reference to its relatively small size. That nickname may be a little misleading, however; the pothos can actually develop long, trailing vines that stretch out for 10 feet or more!&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;There are plenty of reasons why the pothos ranks so highly on our list. One is that the pothos is one of the best plants for purifying the air in your home. The pothos is also an ideal choice for so-called "black thumbs," surviving with minimal care. If you're after an indoor plant that's relatively forgiving, pothos is a good one to keep in mind.&lt;/p&gt;

They're popular among indoor gardeners for a number of reasons, not least their vibrant, fleshy leaves and beautiful color.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Also note that succulents propagate easily; with some varieties, you can literally grow a whole new plant just by tending to one of the leaves from an existing succulent.                       &lt;p&gt;If you're looking for plants that are highly functional, one of the best choices is the &lt;a href="https://www.amazon.com/Costa-Farms-Aloe-Vera-14-Inches/dp/B079D8CRMM/" target="_blank"&gt;aloe vera&lt;/a&gt; plant. As you're probably aware, this plant has amazing anti-inflammatory and anti-bacterial products. Its healing properties make it useful anytime you have a little scrape or burn.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;There are plenty of other reasons to consider adding aloe to your indoor garden, including the fact that it's one of the best bets for purifying the air in your home. And while aloe is fairly easy to care for, it is not a pet-friendly plant, and should definitely be kept out of reach from your four-legged family members.&lt;/p&gt;

                      <h3 data-role="headline">
                       <a href="https://www.amazon.com/Heart-Leaf-Philodendron-Easiest-House/dp/B006RODC1M/" target="_blank">
                        Philodendron
                       </a>
                      </h3>
                      &lt;img type="lazy-image" data-runner-src="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTg1MDM4My9vcmlnaW4ucG5nIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTY2MjAwOTMzNX0.k932dCtOGRx50Tq38lzi8pAgcpzc_0_ddVDbk-fRp8g/img.png?width=980" id="c98ea" class="rm-shortcode" data-rm-shortcode-id="1bcfea95f33479e9ec0ab56381595134" data-rm-shortcode-name="rebelmouse-image" alt="Philodendron"  data-width="400" data-height="400" /&gt;

                      &lt;p&gt;Like the pothos, the &lt;a href="https://www.amazon.com/Heart-Leaf-Philodendron-Easiest-House/dp/B006RODC1M/" target="_blank"&gt;philodendron&lt;/a&gt; is a houseplant that may surprise you: Though it seems compact, it can grow long, trailing vines that span 10 feet or more. Because of this, it's really great for anyone who wants a hanging plant, or something they can put on a high shelf.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;There are other benefits to this plant as well. It's easy to nurture, easy to prune, and it's easy to propagate, if growing more philodendron is something you're interested in. Altogether, this is one of the best indoor plants for those who are new to gardening, or who don't fancy themselves as being especially plant-savvy.&lt;/p&gt;

It gets its name due to the green leaves with irregular banding, which can sometimes resemble the patterns you see on snakeskins.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Beyond the unique aesthetics, the &lt;a href="https://www.amazon.com/Costa-Farms-Sansevieria-Growers-12-Inches/dp/B07TVK6DC2/" target="_blank"&gt;snake plant&lt;/a&gt; is fantastic because it's extremely low-maintenance. Actually, snake plants are well-known for surviving periods of extended drought! Plus, they can filter a lot of chemicals out of the air, significantly improving the indoor air quality in your home. This is definitely an indoor plant that should be on any short list.&lt;/p&gt;

Rest assured that there is nothing "monstrous" about this particular houseplant, beyond the astonishing rate with which it grows and propagates. While we wouldn't say it's zero-maintenance, it's still a fairly easygoing plant.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Even if you have a mixed track record of keeping your plants alive, this one will probably be just fine. Actually, you only need to water your &lt;a href="https://www.amazon.com/AMERICAN-PLANT-EXCHANGE-Split-Philodendron/dp/B07MVY179P/" target="_blank"&gt;monstera&lt;/a&gt; every week or two, and make certain it gets indirect sunlight to see it thrive.&lt;/p&gt;

Even if you don't place any stock in that, money trees can be excellent additions to any indoor garden. They are relatively easy to maintain, they live for a long time, and they look amazing once they really start to grow.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;If you choose a money tree, just be sure to provide some direct sunlight, keep the temperature reasonably warm, and water your plant once a week or so. That's about all it takes for your money tree to grow.&lt;/p&gt;

No matter which one you get, though, you should find that it's incredibly resilient and easy to keep alive. Its bright colors can add a big splash of character to your home garden or living room.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;This is another one of the best houseplants for those who are brand new to indoor gardening, or who worry that they don't have the highest-level skills when it comes to nurturing plants.&lt;/p&gt;

                      &lt;img type="lazy-image" data-runner-src="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTg1MDQxMC9vcmlnaW4ucG5nIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTY3MjI0ODYyM30.7EsDGw6FDwss-DEzuByClzRAYpai0TRi4PVZBEiuCgA/img.png?width=980" id="83101" class="rm-shortcode" data-rm-shortcode-id="daa43b1b1bd720b1f308d4ad308e0ee6" data-rm-shortcode-name="rebelmouse-image" alt="ZZ Plant"  data-width="400" data-height="400" /&gt;

                      </small>
                      <p>
                       costafarms.com
                      </p>
                      &lt;p&gt;The &lt;a href="https://www.amazon.com/Costa-Farms-ZZ-Zamioculcas-White-Natural/dp/B07RJYZ7W3/" target="_blank"&gt;ZZ plant&lt;/a&gt;, or zamioculcas zamiifolia, sports large, almost potato-like rhizomes; that is, it features thick, tall stalks that grow vertically. It also happens to be a really hardy plant that's ideally suited for low-light environments. Note that the rhizomes are so thick because they are used to store water, which allows this plant to survive for a really long time even with inconsistent upkeep.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The ZZ plant is no good if you have pets. However, because it has long symbolized friendship, it can make for a sweet and thoughtful housewarming gift.&lt;/p&gt;

It's sure to be an instant conversation-starter if you bring it into your home garden.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Note that the bird's nest fern fares best in indirect sunlight, as well as in areas that get a lot of humidity. Because of this, many indoor gardeners choose this one to add greenery to their bathroom.&lt;/p&gt;

                      &lt;p&gt;Last but not least, the &lt;a href="https://www.amazon.com/Thorsens-Greenhouse-Lyrata-Fiddle-Indoor/dp/B08QXTDVCY/" target="_blank"&gt;fiddle-leaf fig&lt;/a&gt; (ficus lyrata) is a perfect plant for any indoor gardener who can offer access to some decent sunlight. Looking for a plant to set in the windowsill? This is one of your best bets! It boasts a lovely appearance, though it does require a more experienced gardener.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Unfortunately, the fiddle-leaf fig is &lt;a href="https://www.thesill.com/blogs/plants-101/how-to-care-for-a-fiddle-leaf-fig" target="_blank"&gt;more susceptible&lt;/a&gt; to pests and plant diseases than some other plants, and it can also be sensitive to swings in temperature or humidity. That said, it is a gorgeous plant that will definitely reward you for your attentive care.&lt;/p&gt;

                     &lt;h2&gt;What You'll Need to Grow Houseplants&lt;br&gt;&lt;/h2&gt;&lt;p&gt;Choosing the right kinds of plants is a critical first step toward developing a vibrant indoor garden. But of course, there's some additional equipment you'll want to invest in to make sure you're able to tend to your plants as needed.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;A few of the basic tools to have handy include:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul class="ee-ul"&gt;&lt;li&gt;Watering can&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Hand trowel&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Pruning scissors&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Potting soil*&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Fertilizer*&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;* Note that different plants may require different kinds of soil or fertilizer, so make sure you select the materials best suited to your specific indoor plant life.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h2&gt;What are the Benefits of Indoor Plants?&lt;/h2&gt;&lt;p&gt;No matter which specific houseplants you invest in, your home will benefit from them. Indeed, the benefits of keeping indoor plants are numerous.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul class="ee-ul"&gt;&lt;li&gt;They can clean contaminants out of your air.&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;They can help you achieve a cozy, welcoming vibe in any room.&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Indoor plant life has also been linked with improved mental health.&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Caring for plant life can provide a sense of accomplishment.&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Some plants, such as aloe vera, also come with unique healing effects.&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;These are just a few of the reasons to continue opening your home to some low-maintenance flora.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h2&gt;What are the Easiest Plants to Grow Indoors?&lt;/h2&gt;&lt;p&gt;While some indoor gardeners want a challenge, many of us are simply interested in something we can enjoy with relatively low maintenance; or, at least, something that will prove fairly resilient, should we accidentally forget to water it as promptly as we should.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Some of the easiest indoor plant options include:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul class="ee-ul"&gt;&lt;li&gt;Pothos&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Peace Lily&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Philodendron&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Snake plant&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;ZZ plants&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;If you're looking for something that's truly beginner-friendly, put these plants at the top of your shopping list.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h2&gt;Where Can You Find the Best Houseplants?&lt;/h2&gt;&lt;p&gt;As for indoor plant shopping, there are certainly plenty of options. You can actually have indoor plants shipped to you directly from Amazon, or from more garden-specific e-retailers such as The Sill and Bloomscape.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Alternatively, we recommend spending some time at a local lawn and garden center. There, you can actually see some plants up close and get a good idea of the space they will take up. Plus, you can ask the local pros for any tips, stock up on tools, etc.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Big-box home improvement stores can also be good places to try as you seek indoor plants and equipment.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h2&gt;Turn Your Home Into an Indoor Garden&lt;/h2&gt;&lt;p&gt;One of the great things about indoor gardening is that there's a relatively low threshold for entry. Even if you've never considered it before, you can stock up on a few low-maintenance plants and be well on your way. Why not start with just a single succulent or a couple of pothos plants, and see where things go from there?&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h1&gt;&lt;/h1&gt;&lt;h1&gt;&lt;/h1&gt;&lt;p&gt;Whatever direction you decide to go in, we wish you the best as you reap all the benefits of indoor gardening. Start with any of the plants on this list and you'll be in good shape!&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Josh Hurst &lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/em&gt;&lt;em&gt;is a journalist, critic, and essayist. He lives in Knoxville, TN, with his wife and three sons. He covers natural health, nutrition, supplements, and clean energy. His writing has appeared in Health, Shape, and Remedy Review.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

                  </a>
                 </div>

                 <h2 class="widget__headline h2">
                  <a aria-label="Wild Weather: 4 Essential Reads About Tornadoes and Thunderstorms" class="widget__headline-text custom-post-headline" data-type="text" href="https://www.ecowatch.com/extreme-weather-2651149545.html">
                   Wild Weather: 4 Essential Reads About Tornadoes and Thunderstorms
                  </a>
                 </h2>
                 <div class="social-author clearfix">
                  <div class="social-author__avatar image">
                   <div class="cover-all image" style='background-image: url("https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy82NzI1NTU3L29yaWdpbi5qcGciLCJleHBpcmVzX2F0IjoxNjQ3NTIxOTEwfQ.RRiCDsOja8F3DatceLE6FbT3uo6F9-1QV9_s0V8Hr34/img.jpg?width=210")'>
                   </div>

                  </a>
                 </div>

                  <span class="social-date__text">
                   20 March
                  </span>

                 <a class="widget__section js-load-brick-on-click" href="https://www.ecowatch.com/climate-change/">

                  </script>
                  <div class="body-description">
                   <div class="widget__brief">
                    <p>
                     By Jennifer Weeks
                    </p>
                    <p>
                     <span>
                     </span>
                     Springtime in the U.S. is frequently a season for thunderstorms, which can spawn tornadoes. These large storms are common in the South and Southeast in March and April, then shift toward the Plains states in May. Scientists have warned that 2021 could be an
                     <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/weather/2021/02/25/active-tornado-season-south/" target="_blank">
                      active tornado year
                     </a>
                     , partly because of a La Niña climate pattern in the tropical Pacific Ocean. Past research has suggested that La Niña increases the frequency of tornadoes and hail by concentrating hot, humid air over Texas and other Southern states, which
                     <a href="https://www.climate.gov/news-features/featured-images/el-ni%C3%B1o-and-la-ni%C3%B1a-affect-spring-tornadoes-and-hailstorms" target="_blank">
                      helps to promote storm formation
                     </a>
                     .
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <div class="content-container">
                   </div>
                   <div class="js-appear-on-expand">
                    <template>
                     &lt;p&gt;
	These four articles from The Conversation's archives explain how tornadoes form, why night tornadoes are more deadly, and how in rare cases thunderstorms can take a different but equally destructive form – a derecho. We also look at a neglected aspect of disaster response: disposing of massive quantities of waste.
&lt;/p&gt;
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-1" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/extreme-weather" data-id="1" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651149545" data-published-at="1616203864" id="rebelltitem1">
                      &lt;div id="29763" class="rm-shortcode" data-rm-shortcode-id="b2e3292fb89870453f11f09caf9d5972"&gt;&lt;blockquote class="twitter-tweet twitter-custom-tweet" data-twitter-tweet-id="1371533055916056579" data-partner="rebelmouse"&gt;&lt;div style="margin:1em 0"&gt;An Enhanced risk for fast-moving severe storms, capable of producing several tornadoes (some strong), damaging gust… https://t.co/MraCZVKpgH&lt;/div&gt; &amp;mdash; NWS Storm Prediction Center (@NWS Storm Prediction Center)&lt;a href="https://twitter.com/NWSSPC/statuses/1371533055916056579"&gt;1615833937.0&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
                     </div>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="1-how-thunderstorms-generate-tornadoes" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/extreme-weather" data-id="2" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651149545" data-published-at="1616203864" id="rebelltitem2">
                      <h3 data-role="headline">
                       1. How Thunderstorms Generate Tornadoes
                      </h3>
                      &lt;p&gt;Most tornadoes are spawned by large, intense thunderstorms called supercell thunderstorms. The key ingredients are rising air that rotates, and wind shear – winds at different altitudes blowing at different speeds, and/or from different directions.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Forecasters can't always predict when or where a tornado may form, but they are very good at identifying the conditions that have the potential to support strong tornadoes. As Penn State university meteorologists &lt;a href="https://scholar.google.com/citations?user=T2Ozg5EAAAAJ&amp;amp;hl=en" target="_blank"&gt;Paul Markowski&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href="https://scholar.google.com/citations?user=EUp5dOkAAAAJ&amp;amp;hl=en" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;Yvette Richardson&lt;/a&gt; explain,&lt;/p&gt;&lt;blockquote&gt;"The National Weather Service's Storm Prediction Center routinely predicts large outbreaks days in advance. 'High-risk' outlooks capture most &lt;a href="https://theconversation.com/understanding-tornadoes-5-questions-answered-77448" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;major tornado events&lt;/a&gt;, and strong tornadoes rarely occur outside of tornado watches. We have less ability to forecast tornadoes in more marginal situations, such as within non-supercell storms."&lt;br&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
                     </div>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="2-a-special-risk-in-the-south-night-tornadoes" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/extreme-weather" data-id="3" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651149545" data-published-at="1616203864" id="rebelltitem3">
                      <h3 data-role="headline">
                       2. A Special Risk in the South: Night Tornadoes
                      </h3>
                      &lt;p&gt;Tornado strikes are bad news at any time, but especially when they occur at night. Night tornadoes are more than twice as likely to be fatal as daytime twisters, for several reasons: They are harder for storm spotters to see, people may sleep through alerts, and victims are more likely to be in vulnerable structures such as mobile homes at night.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Night tornadoes are more common in the South because of regional atmospheric conditions there. University of Tennessee geographer &lt;a href="https://scholar.google.com/citations?user=LvpAEa0AAAAJ&amp;amp;hl=en" target="_blank"&gt;Kelsey Ellis&lt;/a&gt; and Middle Tennessee State University geoscientist &lt;a href="https://scholar.google.com/citations?user=BZn_vToAAAAJ&amp;amp;hl=en" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;Alisa Hass&lt;/a&gt; write that communication challenges are a serious problem in their state, where &lt;a href="https://theconversation.com/tornadoes-that-strike-at-night-are-more-deadly-and-require-more-effective-warning-systems-132955" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;nearly half of tornadoes strike at night&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"Experts in Tennessee recommend having multiple methods for receiving warnings at night," they note. "This strategy allows for backup options when power goes out, cellphones go down or other unforeseen circumstances occur."&lt;/p&gt;
                     </div>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-4" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/extreme-weather" data-id="4" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651149545" data-published-at="1616203864" id="rebelltitem4">
                      &lt;span style="display:block;position:relative;padding-top:56.25%;" class="rm-shortcode" data-rm-shortcode-id="2fe8d3ab4997e27b24d082249cd16c79"&gt;&lt;iframe lazy-loadable="true" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/LT7yRMLAkCY?rel=0" width="100%" height="auto"  frameborder="0" scrolling="no" style="position:absolute;top:0;left:0;width:100%;height:100%;"&gt;&lt;/iframe&gt;&lt;/span&gt;
                     </div>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="3-derechos-storms-without-spin" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/extreme-weather" data-id="5" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651149545" data-published-at="1616203864" id="rebelltitem5">
                      <h3 data-role="headline">
                       3. Derechos: Storms Without Spin
                      </h3>
                      &lt;p&gt;In rare instances, weather systems can generate organized lines of thunderstorms called derechos, from the Spanish word for "straight ahead." For a storm to qualify as a derecho, it has to produce winds of 57.5 mph (26 meters per second) or greater. And those intense winds must extend over a path at least 250 miles (400 kilometers) long, with no more than three hours separating individual severe wind reports.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Most areas of the Central and eastern U.S. may experience a derecho once or twice a year on average. They occur mainly from April through August, but they can also occur earlier in spring or later in fall. And they can inflict heavy damage. A derecho that swept across the Midwest in August 2020 generated &lt;a href="https://www.desmoinesregister.com/story/news/2020/10/17/iowas-august-derecho-most-costly-thunderstorm-us-history-7-5-billion-damages/3695053001/" target="_blank"&gt;over US$7.5 billion in damages&lt;/a&gt; – the nation's most costly thunderstorm.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Derechos can be even harder to predict than tornadoes, and once they form, they can move very fast. As Colorado State University atmospheric scientist &lt;a href="https://scholar.google.com/citations?user=vfbhQHkAAAAJ&amp;amp;hl=en" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;Russ Schumacher&lt;/a&gt; warns,&lt;/p&gt;&lt;blockquote&gt;"Communities, first responders and utilities may have only a few hours to prepare for an oncoming derecho, so it is important to know how to receive severe thunderstorm warnings, such as TV, radio and smartphone alerts, and to take these warnings seriously. Tornadoes and tornado warnings often get the most attention, but lines of severe thunderstorms &lt;a href="https://theconversation.com/what-is-a-derecho-an-atmospheric-scientist-explains-these-rare-but-dangerous-storm-systems-140319" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;can also pack a major punch&lt;/a&gt;."&lt;br&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
                     </div>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-6" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/extreme-weather" data-id="6" data-is-image="True" data-post-id="2651149545" data-published-at="1616203864" id="rebelltitem6">
                      &lt;img lazy-loadable="true" data-runner-src="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTg1NDM0OS9vcmlnaW4uanBnIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTY3NjM0MDU5OX0.IIUbc0NrwO7kA3pvPZNMy492syBAjWvS-Q2jM7YlDoA/img.jpg?width=980" id="4937d" class="rm-shortcode" data-rm-shortcode-id="0296c946f4e9eed86b20d54ab2dcc4f0" data-rm-shortcode-name="rebelmouse-image"   data-width="1000" data-height="667" /&gt;
                      <small class="image-media media-photo-credit">
                      </small>
                      <p>
                       <span style="background-color: initial;">
                        An August 2020 derecho crumpled this grain storage tower in Martelle, Iowa.
                       </span>
                       <span style="background-color: initial;">
                        <em>
                         <a href="https://flic.kr/p/2jxjHas" target="_blank">
                          Phil Roeder / Flickr
                         </a>
                         /
                        </em>
                        <a href="https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by/4.0/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
                         <em>
                          CC BY
                         </em>
                        </a>
                       </span>
                      </p>
                     </div>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="4-cleaning-up-after-storms" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/extreme-weather" data-id="7" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651149545" data-published-at="1616203864" id="rebelltitem7">
                      <h3 data-role="headline">
                       4. Cleaning Up After Storms
                      </h3>
                      &lt;p&gt;Tornadoes and other natural disasters often leave huge quantities of debris behind – uprooted trees, splintered buildings, smashed cars and more. It can take communities months or even years to clean up, and the process typically is slow, expensive and dangerous.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href="https://scholar.google.com/citations?user=vUhXX-MAAAAJ&amp;amp;hl=en" target="_blank"&gt;Sybil Derrible&lt;/a&gt; of the University of Illinois–Chicago, &lt;a href="https://scholar.google.com/citations?user=rytzGosAAAAJ&amp;amp;hl=en" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;Juyeong Choi&lt;/a&gt; of Florida State University and &lt;a href="https://scholar.google.com/citations?user=J8dGrPwAAAAJ&amp;amp;hl=en" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;Nazli Yesiller&lt;/a&gt; of California Polytechnic State University study urban engineering, disaster management and planning, and waste management. They see a need for new technologies and strategies that officials can use to figure out what materials storm debris contains and find options for &lt;a href="https://theconversation.com/millions-of-burnt-trees-and-rusted-cars-post-disaster-cleanup-is-expensive-time-consuming-and-wasteful-123566" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;separating, reusing and recycling it&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;blockquote&gt;"For example, drones and autonomous sensing technologies can be combined with artificial intelligence to estimate amounts and quality of debris, the types of materials it contains and how it can be repurposed rapidly. Technologies that allow for fast sorting and separation of mixed materials can also speed up debris management operations," they write.&lt;br&gt;"Turning the problem around, creating new sustainable construction materials – especially in disaster-prone areas – will make it easier to repurpose debris after disasters."&lt;/blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Editor's note: This story is a roundup of articles from The Conversation's archives.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;&lt;a href="https://theconversation.com/us/team#jennifer-weeks" target="_blank"&gt;Jennifer Weeks&lt;/a&gt; is a senior environment + energy editor at The Conversation.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Reposted with permission from &lt;a href="https://theconversation.com/wild-weather-4-essential-reads-about-tornadoes-and-thunderstorms-157275" target="_blank"&gt;The Conversation&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/em&gt; &lt;/p&gt;
                     </div>
                     &lt;script async="async" data-counter="https://counter.theconversation.com/content/157275/count?distributor=republish-lightbox-advanced" id="theconversation_tracker_hook" src="https://theconversation.com/javascripts/lib/content_tracker_hook.js" type="text/javascript"&gt;&lt;/script&gt;

            <div class="widget tag-indoor-gardening tag-indoor-plants tag-gardening tag-houseplants tag-plants post-section--reviews" data-category="Reviews" elid="2651139034">
             <article class="clearfix page-article sm-mb-1 quality-MD post-2651139034" data-is-frozen="false" elid="2651139034">
              <div class="row px10">
               <div class="col sm-mb-1" id="col-center" style="width:100.0%;">
                <div class="widget__head">
                 <a aria-label="The Best Houseplants for Your Indoor Garden" href="https://www.ecowatch.com/best-houseplants-for-indoor-gardens-2651139034.html">

                  <div class="body-description">
                   <div class="widget__brief">
                    <p>
                     By
                     <span style="background-color: initial;">
                      Kenny Stancil
                     </span>
                    </p>
                    <p>
                     <span style="background-color: initial;">
                     </span>
                     Four congressional Democrats on Friday unveiled the BUILD GREEN Infrastructure and Jobs Act, a bill that would invest $500 billion over 10 years in state, local, and tribal projects to galvanize the transition to all electric public transportation — reducing climate-damaging greenhouse gas emissions and health-threatening air pollution while expanding clean mass transit and creating up to one million new jobs.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <div class="content-container">
                   </div>
                   <div class="js-appear-on-expand">
                    <template>
                     &lt;p&gt;Modeled after the Department of Transportation's BUILD grant program, the &lt;a href="https://www.warren.senate.gov/imo/media/doc/BUILD_GREEN_Act%20Summary.pdf" target="_blank"&gt;bill&lt;/a&gt; to provide grant funding to green the nation's public transportation infrastructure while creating good-paying jobs in the process was introduced by Sens. Elizabeth Warren (D-Mass.) and Ed Markey (D-Mass.) as well as Reps. Andrew Levin (D-Mich.) and Alexandria Ocasio-Cortez (D-N.Y.). &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"The climate crisis is an existential threat to our planet," Warren &lt;a href="https://andylevin.house.gov/media/press-releases/levin-warren-markey-and-ocasio-cortez-unveil-build-green-infrastructure-and" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;acknowledged&lt;/a&gt; in a press release, "but it's also a once-in-a-generation opportunity to rebuild our crumbling infrastructure, create a million good new jobs, and unleash the best of American innovation."&lt;/p&gt;
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-1" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/build-green-act" data-id="1" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651149717" data-published-at="1616205688" id="rebelltitem1">
                      &lt;p&gt;The BUILD GREEN Act, she added, "will make the big federal investments necessary to transform our country's transportation system, confront the racial and economic inequality embedded in our fossil fuel economy, and achieve the ambitious targets for 100% clean energy in America."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;That assessment was shared by Markey, who &lt;a href="https://andylevin.house.gov/media/press-releases/levin-warren-markey-and-ocasio-cortez-unveil-build-green-infrastructure-and" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;said&lt;/a&gt; that "we cannot build back better without building back greener." Markey called the bill "our opportunity to invest in a clean energy revolution across our country, transform our transportation sector to be climate-smart, and create millions of good-paying union jobs at the same time."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"We can work together," he added, "to leverage investment in climate action, reduce emissions, and support environmental justice communities through bold infrastructure projects, all while tackling our climate crisis."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Co-sponsors of the &lt;a href="https://www.warren.senate.gov/imo/media/doc/BUILD%20GREEN%20Bill%20Text.pdf" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;proposed legislation&lt;/a&gt; — which is supported by almost three in five Americans, according to a new &lt;a href="https://www.filesforprogress.org/datasets/2021/3/dfp_build_green_act_toplines.pdf" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;poll &lt;/a&gt;(pdf) conducted by Data for Progress—include Sen. Bernie Sanders (I-Vt.) and Reps. Jan Schakowsky (D-Ill.), Pramila Jayapal (D-Wash.), Ayanna Pressley (D-Mass.), Rashida Tlaib (D-Mich.), Mondaire Jones (D-N.Y.), and Jamaal Bowman (D-N.Y.), among others.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Alluding to the recent &lt;a href="https://www.commondreams.org/news/2021/02/18/forget-ted-cruz-whats-really-missing-texas-green-new-deal" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;crisis in Texas&lt;/a&gt; caused by the collision of a &lt;a href="https://www.commondreams.org/news/2021/02/16/failed-state-power-outages-amid-freezing-weather-texas-threaten-lives-and-covid" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;deregulated&lt;/a&gt;, fossil-fuel dependent energy system and a climate change-driven &lt;a href="https://www.commondreams.org/news/2021/02/17/role-climate-crisis-cant-be-hand-waved-away-scientists-say-freezing-texas-linked" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;winter storm&lt;/a&gt;, Ocasio-Cortez &lt;a href="https://andylevin.house.gov/media/press-releases/levin-warren-markey-and-ocasio-cortez-unveil-build-green-infrastructure-and" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;said &lt;/a&gt;that "we must stop spending billions of taxpayer money on infrastructure systems only for them to fail at the most crucial moment."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"The BUILD GREEN Act," Ocasio-Cortez continued, "helps ensure that our federal dollars are being invested in infrastructure that can sustain the impact of climate change and better prepares our communities for extreme weather events."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"In most of the country," she added, "subways, buses, and other public transit are practically inaccessible or completely overburdened," meaning that "this bill would make a dramatic, material difference in the everyday lives of hundreds of millions of people."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Calling the electrification of personal vehicles and mass transit a "central pillar" of the Green New Deal resolution &lt;a href="https://www.commondreams.org/news/2019/02/07/major-party-backing-ocasio-cortez-and-markey-unveil-green-new-deal-outlining-wwii" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;introduced&lt;/a&gt; in 2019 by Ocasio-Cortez and Markey, Levin &lt;a href="https://andylevin.house.gov/media/press-releases/levin-warren-markey-and-ocasio-cortez-unveil-build-green-infrastructure-and" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;said&lt;/a&gt; that "the answer to both the climate crisis and the crisis of wealth inequality is to empower working people with the sustainable investments necessary to rebuild the communities devastated by decades of pollution and corporate trade policy."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;He added that the bill "will deliver the transformational change demanded by the American people while ensuring that we build the green economy of the 21st century here at home with good-paying, union jobs."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The Better Utilizing Investments to Leverage Development and Generating Renewable Energy to Electrify the Nation's (BUILD GREEN) Infrastructure and Jobs Act would:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;jumpstart the transition to all electric public transportation, expand clean mass transit to underserved communities, and help modernize our crumbling infrastructure by covering up to 85% of costs for eligible state, local, and tribal projects, with an option for the Secretary of Transportation to cover 100% of costs;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;reduce carbon emissions by an estimated 21.5 million metric tons of CO2 annually or the equivalent of taking 4.5 million combustion engine cars off the road;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;prevent an estimated 4,200 deaths annually by reducing significant sources of local air pollution that cause adverse health effects like asthma, and avert $100 billion annually in healthcare costs;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;start to correct decades of health disparities and environmental injustice by dedicating at least 40% of all funding to projects in frontline, vulnerable, and disadvantaged communities; and&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;create up to one million good new jobs with strong labor protections.&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;In its &lt;a href="https://www.dataforprogress.org/memos/electrifying-transportation" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;evaluation&lt;/a&gt; of the economic and environmental impacts of the bill, which it called "a vital component of tackling the climate crisis," Data for Progress estimated that electrifying the nation's public transportation systems, installing electric vehicle charging infrastructure nationwide, and expanding associated renewable energy generation capacity would save lives and money.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The proposed legislation is endorsed by a slew of progressive advocacy groups, including Data for Progress as well as Sunrise Movement, League of Conservation Voters, Natural Resources Defense Council, Sierra Club, 350.org, Greenpeace, Public Citizen, Friends of the Earth, Center for Progressive Reform, GreenLatinos, Rewiring America, New Consensus, Zero Hour, and WE ACT for Environmental Justice.&lt;/p&gt;
                     </div>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-2" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/build-green-act" data-id="2" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651149717" data-published-at="1616205688" id="rebelltitem2">
                      &lt;p&gt;Given that "transportation represents about 29% of U.S. emissions," &lt;a href="https://andylevin.house.gov/media/press-releases/levin-warren-markey-and-ocasio-cortez-unveil-build-green-infrastructure-and" target="_blank"&gt;said&lt;/a&gt; Natalie Mebane, U.S. policy director at 350.org, "we can make huge progress in lowering our greenhouse gas emissions by electrifying the transportation sector and ensuring that it is powered by 100% clean energy."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;A recent assessment of President Joe Biden's climate plans &lt;a href="https://www.commondreams.org/news/2021/03/11/researchers-say-true-climate-leadership-us-would-be-60-emissions-reduction-2030" target="_blank"&gt;found&lt;/a&gt; his transportation policies to be inadequate if the U.S. is to reach his administration's goal of net-zero emissions by 2050.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Mebane added that "this bill will create close to one million jobs at a time when we need a just economic recovery immediately" in the wake of the devastating Covid-19 pandemic and corresponding economic crisis.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Robert R.M. Verchick, president of the board of directors of the Center for Progressive Reform and professor of environmental law at Loyola University, New Orleans, &lt;a href="https://andylevin.house.gov/media/press-releases/levin-warren-markey-and-ocasio-cortez-unveil-build-green-infrastructure-and" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;said&lt;/a&gt; that "the transportation networks we build today shape the possibilities for tomorrow."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"If we want our children and grandchildren to thrive in their schools and in their jobs, they will need ways to get there," said Verchick. "If we want neighborhoods free of smog and industrial racket, we will need clean and efficient ways of moving around. Few investments we make today will have as profound an impact on the opportunities available to future generations as our infrastructure choices."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The BUILD GREEN Act was unveiled just two weeks after Sunrise Movement &lt;a href="https://www.commondreams.org/news/2021/03/05/good-jobs-all-sunrise-movement-launches-campaign-fight-climate-crisis-work-guarantee" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;launched&lt;/a&gt; its "Good Jobs for All" campaign to put the country on a path toward a Green New Deal; that happened not long after Pressley introduced the &lt;a href="https://www.commondreams.org/news/2021/02/18/demanding-dignified-work-and-living-wage-legal-rights-ayanna-pressley-unveils-jobs" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;Federal Job Guarantee Resolution&lt;/a&gt;, which seeks to make "meaningful, dignified work" at a livable wage an enforceable legal right.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Earlier this week, hundreds of local officials across the nation &lt;a href="https://www.commondreams.org/news/2021/03/16/hundreds-local-officials-demand-transformative-infrastructure-plan-us" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;called on&lt;/a&gt; the Biden administration and Congress to deliver a bold infrastructure plan that improves the health of communities across the country.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Sanders, for his part, &lt;a href="https://twitter.com/SenSanders/status/1372619319344050178" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;said &lt;/a&gt;Thursday that if Republicans try to obstruct progress on green jobs and infrastructure, Democrats "must use our majority to get it done."&lt;/p&gt;
                     </div>
                     &lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Reposted with permission from &lt;a href="https://www.commondreams.org/news/2021/03/19/democrats-unveil-build-green-infrastructure-and-jobs-act" target="_blank"&gt;Common Dreams&lt;/a&gt;. &lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

                 <h2 class="widget__headline h2">
                  <a aria-label="Mysterious Circling Behavior Observed in Large Marine Animals" class="widget__headline-text custom-post-headline" data-type="text" href="https://www.ecowatch.com/mysterious-circling-behavior-observed-in-several-large-marine-animals-2651144730.html">
                   Mysterious Circling Behavior Observed in Large Marine Animals
                  </a>
                 </h2>
                 <div class="social-author clearfix">

true, "new_amp": "\u003camp-ad width=336 height=280\n    type=\"doubleclick\"\n    data-slot=\"/5376056/ecowatch_content_9_amp\"\n    data-multi-size=\"320x50,300x250\"\u003e\n\u003c/amp-ad\u003e", "order": 9}, {"amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "display": true, "new_amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "order": 10}], "adsOrder": [2]}
                  </script>
                  <div class="body-description">
                   <div class="widget__brief">
                    <p>
                     Several large marine
                     <a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/animals/" target="_self">
                      animals
                     </a>
                     , from
                     <a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/sharks" target="_self">
                      sharks
                     </a>
                     to
                     <a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/sharks" target="_self">
                      seals
                     </a>
                     to
                     <a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/sea-turtles" target="_self">
                      turtles
                     </a>
                     to
                     <a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/penguins" target="_self">
                      penguins
                     </a>
                     , have been observed doing something scientists find strange: swimming in circles.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <div class="content-container">
                   </div>
                   <div class="js-appear-on-expand">
                    <template>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-1" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/mysterious-circling-behavior-observed-in-several-large-marine-animals" data-id="1" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651144730" data-published-at="1616194774" id="rebelltitem1">
                      &lt;p&gt;The observations, published in &lt;a href="https://www.cell.com/iscience/fulltext/S2589-0042(21)00189-9" target="_blank"&gt;iScience Thursday&lt;/a&gt;, raise further questions about why exactly so many &lt;a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/ocean" target="_self"&gt;ocean&lt;/a&gt; animals are moving in a seemingly inefficient way.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"Given that similar circling behavior was observed across a wide variety of marine megafauna taxa, it might be possible that it is a behavioral convergence having similar purposes," lead author Tomoko Narazaki, from the University of Tokyo, told &lt;a href="https://gizmodo.com/scientists-dont-know-why-all-these-sea-creatures-are-sw-1846503767" target="_blank"&gt;Gizmodo&lt;/a&gt;. "But, for now, the purpose and the function of this behavior remain unknown."&lt;/p&gt;
                     </div>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-2" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/mysterious-circling-behavior-observed-in-several-large-marine-animals" data-id="2" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651144730" data-published-at="1616194774" id="rebelltitem2">
                      &lt;p&gt;The behavior was first discovered by accident, as &lt;a href="https://www.newscientist.com/article/2271409-sea-turtles-sharks-and-king-penguins-swim-in-mysterious-circles/" target="_blank"&gt;New Scientist explained&lt;/a&gt;. Narazaki was studying the navigational abilities of green sea turtles (&lt;em&gt;Chelonia mydas&lt;/em&gt;) in the Indian and Pacific oceans. Her team moved the turtles away from their breeding grounds to test their ability to find their way home again, but they noticed something odd. When the turtles were about to approach the waters off of their nesting beaches, they began to circle. One made 76 rotations lasting 16 to 20 seconds each.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;At first, Narazaki said, she thought the tracking equipment was broken.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"To be honest, I doubted my eyes when I first saw the data because the turtle circles so constantly, just like a machine!" Narazaki said in a &lt;a href="https://phys.org/news/2021-03-enigmatic-circling-behavior-captured-whales.html" target="_blank"&gt;Cell Press release published by Phys.org&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
                     </div>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-3" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/mysterious-circling-behavior-observed-in-several-large-marine-animals" data-id="3" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651144730" data-published-at="1616194774" id="rebelltitem3">
                      &lt;p&gt;The detailed observation of the turtles' movements was enabled by a new tracking technology that has made possible a 3D modeling of an animal's movements down to the meter and the second, as the study explained.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"When I got back in my lab, I reported this interesting discovery to my colleagues who use the same 3D data loggers to study a wide range of marine megafauna taxa," Narazaki further told Cell Press.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;These researchers reported that they also had observed the strange behavior in species from tiger sharks to king penguins to Antarctic fur seals, as Gizmodo reported.&lt;/p&gt;
                     </div>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-4" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/mysterious-circling-behavior-observed-in-several-large-marine-animals" data-id="4" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651144730" data-published-at="1616194774" id="rebelltitem4">
                      &lt;p&gt;It is more efficient for an animal to swim in a straight line in order to reach its destination, so why is this behavior so common? The researchers have several ideas.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;One possibility is that the animals circle in order to forage for food. Four tiger sharks, for example, circled 272 times in their known feeding grounds off Hawaii, the study authors wrote. However, some of the circling behavior seems clearly not related to eating. One male tiger shark circled before approaching a female, according to Gizmodo. However, seals, penguins and Cuvier's beaked whales all circled near the surface of the water, when normally they feed farther down, according to New Scientist. In addition, fur seals normally circled during the day, while they typically feed at night, Cell Press noted.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;It is also possible that some animals circle to help with navigation.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"What surprised me most was that homing &lt;a href="https://phys.org/tags/turtles/" target="_blank"&gt;turtles&lt;/a&gt; undertake circling behavior at seemingly navigationally important locations, such as just before the final approach to their goal," Narazaki told Cell Press.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;It is possible that the circling helps turtles detect magnetic fields, a technique that submarines also use when making geomagnetic observations. Previous research has suggested that turtles are capable of sensing magnetic fields, according to New Scientist.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;But for now, the circling ultimately remains another mystery of the ocean.&lt;/p&gt;
                     </div>
                    </template>
                   </div>
