                  <a aria-label="Murder Hornet Season Is Coming: Scientists Worried About Honey Bees Ask the Public for Help" class="widget__headline-text custom-post-headline" data-type="text" href="https://www.ecowatch.com/murder-hornet-season-honey-bees-2651148157.html">
                   Murder Hornet Season Is Coming: Scientists Worried About Honey Bees Ask the Public for Help
                  </a>

                  <div class="body-description">
                   <div class="widget__brief">
                    <p>
                     The so-called
                     <a href="https://www.nytimes.com/2020/05/02/us/asian-giant-hornet-washington.html" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
                      murder hornet
                     </a>
                     , known for its "excruciating" sting and ability to wipe out an entire bee-colony in just a few hours, is coming out of hibernation and scientists need help in eradicating them,
                     <a href="https://www.vice.com/en/article/qjpy5m/west-coast-scientists-encourage-public-to-set-traps-for-murder-hornets" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
                      VICE reported
                     </a>
                     .
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <div class="content-container">
                   </div>
                   <div class="js-appear-on-expand">
                    <template>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-1" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/murder-hornet-season-honey-bees" data-id="1" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651148157" data-published-at="1616191182" id="rebelltitem1">
                      &lt;p&gt;Scientists in the U.S. and Canada announced a "war" against the murder hornet as it begins to establish its nests in spring, &lt;a href="https://apnews.com/article/us-canada-scientists-set-to-battle-murder-hornets-96085eb31e9b70070e0ae21a5752a14e" target="_blank"&gt;AP reported&lt;/a&gt;. Over the past two years, the world's largest hornets have been spotted in British Columbia and Washington state.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"This is not a species we want to tolerate here in the United States," Sven-Erik Spichiger of the Washington state Department of Agriculture said, according to AP. "We may not get them all, but we will get as many as we can."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Scientists are encouraging citizens to begin setting up an orange juice or a brown sugar-based trap in July, The Washington State Department of Agriculture wrote in a &lt;a href="https://agr.wa.gov/about-wsda/news-and-media-relations/news-releases?article=32279" target="_blank"&gt;statement&lt;/a&gt;. Residents in Whatcom, Skagit, San Juan, Island, Jefferson, and Clallam counties are especially encouraged to participate.&lt;/p&gt;
                     </div>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-2" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/murder-hornet-season-honey-bees" data-id="2" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651148157" data-published-at="1616191182" id="rebelltitem2">
                      &lt;p&gt;While the department and several agencies, including Washington State University, are planning their own eradication efforts, citizen reportings are necessary to cover as much ground as possible. Last year, half of the confirmed reports of the murder hornet in Washington and all confirmed reports in British Columbia were from members of the public, the department wrote.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;While the murder hornet, more commonly known as the Asian giant hornet, is rarely deadly, its venom can damage human tissue if stung, &lt;a href="https://www.cnn.com/2021/03/17/us/asian-giant-hornet-season-2021-trnd/index.html" target="_blank"&gt;CNN reported&lt;/a&gt;. "It's an absolutely serious danger to our health and well-being," Paul van Westendorp of the British Columbia Ministry of Agriculture, Food and Fisheries told AP. "These are intimidating insects."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The hornets kill at most a few dozen people a year in Asian countries, according to AP. At the same time, hornets, wasps and bees found in the U.S. kill an average of 62 people a year, AP reported.&lt;/p&gt;
                     </div>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-3" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/murder-hornet-season-honey-bees" data-id="3" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651148157" data-published-at="1616191182" id="rebelltitem3">
                      &lt;p&gt;But the giant insect is not after humans, posing instead a more serious threat to bee populations. Just a small group of Asian giant hornets, for example, can destroy an entire honey bee hive in a few hours, AP reported.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"During one recorded slaughter examined by researchers, each hornet killed one bee every 14 seconds, using powerful mandibles to decapitate its prey," &lt;a href="https://www.nytimes.com/2020/05/03/us/murder-hornets-asian-giant-hornet-bees.html" target="_blank"&gt;The New York Times reported.&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;In a state that relies on honey bees to pollinate its multibillion-dollar agricultural industry, beekeepers and entomologists in Washington worry for the future if the murder hornet is able to establish itself in North America.&lt;/p&gt;
                     </div>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-4" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/murder-hornet-season-honey-bees" data-id="4" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651148157" data-published-at="1616191182" id="rebelltitem4">
                      &lt;p&gt;"Most people are scared to get stung by them," Ruthie Danielsen, a beekeeper in Birch Bay, Washington &lt;a href="https://www.nytimes.com/2020/05/02/us/asian-giant-hornet-washington.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;told The New York Times&lt;/a&gt;. "We're scared that they are going to totally destroy our hives."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Additional efforts to eradicate the giant insect include conducting genome sequencing to find out how the Asian giant hornet first arrived in North America and if there are any subpopulations, VICE reported. "Knowing the origin is important to control efforts because it may offer a better understanding of nesting biology and potential range, which varies in native populations," Anna Childers, a researcher at the U.S. Department of Agriculture, told VICE.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Scientists and department workers plan to catch the live hornet, tag it and track it back to its nest to then be destroyed, VICE reported. "So hanging a trap actually protects you. It lets you know that there's something in the area and contains it in such a way that you can then call [authorities in B.C. or Washington] and we can do something about it." Spichiger told VICE.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Washington residents can report all sightings of Asian giant hornets to WSDA at agr.wa.gov/hornets, via email at
                      <a class="__cf_email__" data-cfemail="3850574a565d4c4b78595f4a164f59165f574e" href="/cdn-cgi/l/email-protection">
                       [email protected]
                      </a>
                      , or by calling 1-800-443-6684.&lt;/p&gt;
                     </div>

                  <a aria-label="'Plague' of Mice Ravages New South Wales Farms" class="widget__headline-text custom-post-headline" data-type="text" href="https://www.ecowatch.com/australia-mice-invasion-farms-2651145074.html">
                   'Plague' of Mice Ravages New South Wales Farms
                  </a>
                 </h2>
                 <div class="social-author clearfix">

                  <div class="body-description">
                   <div class="widget__brief">
                    <p>
                     Rural communities in the Australian state of New South Wales are battling a "plague" of mice that has struck the region.
                    </p>
                   </div>
                   <div class="content-container">
                   </div>
                   <div class="js-appear-on-expand">
                    <template>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-1" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/australia-mice-invasion-farms" data-id="1" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651145074" data-published-at="1616184228" id="rebelltitem1">
                      &lt;p&gt;Thousands of mice are invading grain silos, barns and homes and infesting the farmers' bumper grain harvest.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Mice numbers boomed after &lt;a href="https://www.dw.com/en/heavy-flash-floods-batter-australia-as-cyclone-uesi-is-set-to-hit-the-country/a-52360733" target="_blank"&gt;unusually heavy summer rains&lt;/a&gt; fell across eastern Australia &lt;a href="https://www.dw.com/en/indigenous-australians-fight-coal-and-climate-change/a-39325243" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;after years of drought,&lt;/a&gt; experts explained.&lt;/p&gt;
                     </div>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-2" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/australia-mice-invasion-farms" data-id="2" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651145074" data-published-at="1616184228" id="rebelltitem2">
                      &lt;h3&gt;Farmers Share Mice 'Plague' Impact on Social Media&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;Videos captured on the Moeris family farm in Gilgandra — a five-hour drive northwest of Sydney — show thousands of mice scurrying from under pipes, through storage columns and over machinery.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"Winter crop sowing is at risk and there is a human health impact," the NSW Young Farmers association warned in a tweet, alongside a video showing mice running through hay bales.&lt;/p&gt;
                     </div>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-3" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/australia-mice-invasion-farms" data-id="3" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651145074" data-published-at="1616184228" id="rebelltitem3">
                      &lt;div id="683be" class="rm-shortcode" data-rm-shortcode-id="cc04a23c9def8ad5eb131944a6188eea"&gt;&lt;blockquote class="twitter-tweet twitter-custom-tweet" data-twitter-tweet-id="1371955182129455105" data-partner="rebelmouse"&gt;&lt;div style="margin:1em 0"&gt;#Mice numbers are exploding in many parts of NSW. Haystacks are being destroyed, silos invaded, winter crop sowing… https://t.co/leJr2VXuIj&lt;/div&gt; &amp;mdash; NSW Young Farmers (@NSW Young Farmers)&lt;a href="https://twitter.com/NSWYF/statuses/1371955182129455105"&gt;1615934579.0&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
                     </div>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-4" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/australia-mice-invasion-farms" data-id="4" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651145074" data-published-at="1616184228" id="rebelltitem4">
                      &lt;p&gt;"Mice are still causing nightmares for farmers and rural communities," the NSW Farmers association tweeted.&lt;/p&gt;
                     </div>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-5" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/australia-mice-invasion-farms" data-id="5" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651145074" data-published-at="1616184228" id="rebelltitem5">
                      &lt;div id="06fcc" class="rm-shortcode" data-rm-shortcode-id="fe2e53b514262500b43a1936d0487163"&gt;&lt;blockquote class="twitter-tweet twitter-custom-tweet" data-twitter-tweet-id="1371242488992727046" data-partner="rebelmouse"&gt;&lt;div style="margin:1em 0"&gt;Mice are still causing nightmares for farmers and rural communities in many parts of NSW, as evidenced by this frid… https://t.co/gORpjIjGx2&lt;/div&gt; &amp;mdash; NSW Farmers (@NSW Farmers)&lt;a href="https://twitter.com/NSWFarmers/statuses/1371242488992727046"&gt;1615764660.0&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
                     </div>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-6" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/australia-mice-invasion-farms" data-id="6" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651145074" data-published-at="1616184228" id="rebelltitem6">
                      &lt;p&gt;"At night... the ground is just moving with thousands and thousands of mice just running around" farmer Ron Mckay told the Australian Broadcasting Corporation (ABC).&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h3&gt;The Impact of the Mice Plague&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;Australia's ABC reported three hospital patients in regional New South Wales have been bitten by mice.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;There was one report of a rare mouse-related illness known as lymphocytic choriomeningitis [LCM] in the region, ABC reported, quoting the region's Western Local Health District.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Farmers are also concerned the mice will destroy this year's harvest.&lt;/p&gt;
                     </div>
                     <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-7" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/australia-mice-invasion-farms" data-id="7" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651145074" data-published-at="1616184228" id="rebelltitem7">
                      &lt;h3&gt;How Farmers Plan to Combat the Mice&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;Farmers in New South Wales (NSW) have asked the government for help to combat the "drastic increase" in mice.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The NSW Farmers Association wants emergency permission to lay down the pesticide zinc phosphide to treat their grain.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"This mice situation is only getting worse," NSW Farmers President James Jackson said.&lt;/p&gt;
                     </div>
                     &lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Reposted with permission from &lt;a href="https://www.dw.com/en/australia-plague-of-mice-ravages-new-south-wales/a-56926480" target="_blank"&gt;DW&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

                   <div class="body-description">
                    <div class="widget__brief">
                     <p>
                      Reddit investors have found a way to meme for good.
                     </p>
                    </div>
                    <div class="content-container">
                    </div>
                    <div class="js-appear-on-expand">
                     <template>
                      <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-1" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/reddit-gamestop-adopt-endangered-animals" data-id="1" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651143227" data-published-at="1616174608" id="rebelltitem1">
                       &lt;p&gt;The amateur investors on subreddit WallStreetBets often refer to themselves as apes and use the phrase "Apes Together Strong," &lt;a href="https://www.bbc.com/news/technology-56438230" target="_blank"&gt;BBC News reported&lt;/a&gt;. Now, some subreddit members have started to take this saying literally. Within days, Redditors have raised $350,000 for the Dian Fossey Gorilla Fund by adopting more than 3,500 &lt;a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/gorillas" target="_self"&gt;gorillas&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="https://www.theguardian.com/environment/2021/mar/18/reddit-investors-use-gamestop-proceeds-adopt-thousands-gorillas-aoe" target="_blank"&gt;The Guardian reported&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"It's safe to say that the&lt;a href="https://twitter.com/hashtag/investor?src=hashtag_click" target="_blank"&gt; #investor&lt;/a&gt; community on&lt;a href="https://twitter.com/reddit" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt; @reddit&lt;/a&gt; is not traditionally who we think of as our supporter base. But they definitely surprised and overwhelmed us over the weekend," the &lt;a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/conservation" target="_self"&gt;conservation&lt;/a&gt; group &lt;a href="https://twitter.com/SavingGorillas/status/1371507415754145793" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;tweeted&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
                      </div>
                      <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-5" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/reddit-gamestop-adopt-endangered-animals" data-id="5" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651143227" data-published-at="1616174608" id="rebelltitem5">
                       <h3 data-role="headline">
                       </h3>
                       &lt;div id="b71c8" class="rm-shortcode" data-rm-shortcode-id="d825842c821a0b3eba02ee4674a7cd3b"&gt;&lt;blockquote class="twitter-tweet twitter-custom-tweet" data-twitter-tweet-id="1371507415754145793" data-partner="rebelmouse"&gt;&lt;div style="margin:1em 0"&gt;🚨WE HAVE NEWS 🚨 It’s safe to say that the #investor community on @reddit is not traditionally who we think of as ou… https://t.co/f3Vg6e44dv&lt;/div&gt; &amp;mdash; Dian Fossey Gorilla Fund (@Dian Fossey Gorilla Fund)&lt;a href="https://twitter.com/SavingGorillas/statuses/1371507415754145793"&gt;1615827823.0&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
                      </div>
                      <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-6" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/reddit-gamestop-adopt-endangered-animals" data-id="6" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651143227" data-published-at="1616174608" id="rebelltitem6">
                       &lt;p&gt;The trend began last Friday when Reddit user Pakistani_in_MURICA &lt;a href="https://www.reddit.com/r/wallstreetbets/comments/m3w2jj/adopted_a_gorilla/" target="_blank"&gt;posted&lt;/a&gt; an adoption certificate for a mountain gorilla named Urungano. The post received a 92 percent upvote rate and prompted many other users to follow suit.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The Dian Fossey Gorilla Fund works with mountain gorillas in Rwanda and Grauer's gorillas in the Democratic Republic of Congo, according to BBC News. On Twitter, the group said that the new funds would support their work studying and monitoring gorillas, and supporting the people who live near them.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The organization told The Guardian that it usually receives 20 new gorilla adoptions a weekend, a far cry from the thousands that the Redditors initiated.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"The support that has come to our organization, as well as others, is amazing," Tara Stoinski, the fund's president, chief executive and chief scientific officer, told The Guardian. "One of the biggest challenges in conservation is just that there's not enough funding for the challenges we face on the ground."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The Redditors have also donated to other organizations and adopted other species. The Ape Cognition and Conservation Initiative, which studies &lt;a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/endangered-species" target="_self"&gt;endangered&lt;/a&gt; bonobos, said it received $4,500 from the WallStreetBets community.&lt;/p&gt;
                      </div>
                      <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-9" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/reddit-gamestop-adopt-endangered-animals" data-id="9" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651143227" data-published-at="1616174608" id="rebelltitem9">
                       <h3 data-role="headline">
                       </h3>
                       &lt;div id="b0bdc" class="rm-shortcode" data-rm-shortcode-id="2717617a090516df74e5daa6ac8396bb"&gt;&lt;blockquote class="twitter-tweet twitter-custom-tweet" data-twitter-tweet-id="1372212913100972038" data-partner="rebelmouse"&gt;&lt;div style="margin:1em 0"&gt;Wow!! Thanks to the @Official_WSB community, we have raised $4,500 and bonobos are now featured in @Newsweek! We ar… https://t.co/mlFI4en5Y5&lt;/div&gt; &amp;mdash; Ape Cognition and Conservation Initiative (@Ape Cognition and Conservation Initiative)&lt;a href="https://twitter.com/ApeInitiative/statuses/1372212913100972038"&gt;1615996027.0&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
                      </div>
                      <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-10" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/reddit-gamestop-adopt-endangered-animals" data-id="10" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651143227" data-published-at="1616174608" id="rebelltitem10">
                       &lt;p&gt;The Redditors have also moved beyond apes to adopt endangered animals such as elephants, pangolins and sea turtles, according to The Guardian. The Sheldrick Wildlife Trust, which runs a sanctuary for orphaned elephants in Kenya, experienced a $10,000 rise in donations over the weekend.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"It's a new supporter base for us, for sure, one that we're extremely thankful for," the trust's Amie Alden told The Guardian. "We've currently got more than 90 dependent orphaned elephants in our care and it's an expensive undertaking."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The WallStreetBets community first rose to fame in January, when they noticed that hedge funds were betting against stocks, including GameStop and AMC, and banded together to buy several stocks to boost their prices, &lt;a href="https://www.businessinsider.com/redditors-reddit-money-donate-adopt-apes-gorillas-gamestop-2021-3" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;Business Insider explained&lt;/a&gt;. This caused the share price of GameStop to skyrocket from less than $5 a share at the end of December to more than $450 by Jan. 28, forcing some hedge funds to close their bets at a loss. Some of the Redditors referenced the saga by making their animal donations in the name of GameStop or "Jim Cramer's Tears," The Guardian noted.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"This is the sort of thing that happens when people unaccustomed to having money suddenly get some," BBC News reported one Redditor saying.&lt;/p&gt;
                      </div>

                   <div class="body-description">
                    <div class="widget__brief">
                     <p>
                      By Michael Svoboda
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      To honor Women's History Month, Yale Climate Connections's March bookshelf presents a selection of new and recent titles on how women are changing the politics and prospects for action on climate change.
                     </p>
                    </div>
                    <div class="content-container">
                    </div>
                    <div class="js-appear-on-expand">
                     <template>
                      <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-1" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/climate-change-books-women" data-id="1" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651143464" data-published-at="1616167731" id="rebelltitem1">
                       &lt;p&gt;Three books focus on the efforts of young women. Another four books offer the seasoned perspectives of veteran activists, organizers, and/or journalists, including Jane Fonda and Elizabeth Kolbert.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Rounding out the collection are a natural history/memoir by New York Times columnist Margaret Renkl, two cli-fi novels, an academic appraisal of "the new climate activism," and an NGO report on the importance of gender diversity for climate innovation.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;As always, the descriptions of the works listed below are drawn from copy provided by the publishers or organizations that released them. When two dates of publication are listed, the latter is for the paperback edition.&lt;/p&gt;
                      </div>
                      <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-2" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/climate-change-books-women" data-id="2" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651143464" data-published-at="1616167731" id="rebelltitem2">
                       &lt;p&gt;&lt;a target="_blank" href="https://www.haymarketbooks.org/books/1518-no-planet-b" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;No Planet B: A Teen Vogue Guide to the Climate Crisis&lt;/a&gt;, edited by Lucy Diavolo (Haymarket Books 2021, 248 pages, $15.95 paperback)&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;As the political classes watch our world burn, a new movement of young people is rising to meet the challenge of climate catastrophe. An urgent call for climate justice from Teen Vogue, one of this generation's leading voices, this book is a guide, a toolkit, a warning and a cause for hope.&lt;br&gt;"I hope that this book embodies Teen Vogue's motto of making young people feel seen and heard all over the world. I hope that it forces their parents, communities, loved ones, friends, and – most importantly – those in power to see that the health of our planet depends on how quickly and drastically we change our behaviors. I hope it forces them all to respond." – From the foreword by Teen Vogue editor-in-chief, Lindsay Peoples Wagner&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;&lt;/em&gt;&lt;a target="_blank" href="https://www.chicagoreviewpress.com/girl-warriors-products-9781641603713.php"&gt;Girl Warriors: How 25 Young Activists Are Saving the World&lt;/a&gt;, by Rachel Sarah (Chicago Review Press 2021, 192 pages, $16.99 paperback)&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Girl Warriors tells the stories of 25 climate leaders under age 25. These fearless girls and young women from all over the world are standing up to demand change when no one else is. They've led hundreds of thousands of people in climate strikes, founded non-profits, given TED talks, and sued their governments. A rousing call to action, this book will leave you feeling hopeful that we can make a difference in an age of turmoil, destruction, and uncertainty. "It gives me true hope to read about the phenomenal young women of Girl Warriors. Their fierce commitment to the future of our precious planet is as inspiring as it is vital." – Kate Schatz, New York Times bestselling author of Rad American Women A-Z and Rad Women Worldwide&lt;/em&gt;&lt;em&gt;(&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Editor's note: YCC's &lt;a href="https://yaleclimateconnections.org/2020/03/15-books-about-women-leading-the-way-on-climate-change/" target="_blank"&gt;March 2020 bookshelf&lt;/a&gt; included seven titles by or about Greta Thunberg.)&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
                      </div>
                      <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-3" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/climate-change-books-women" data-id="3" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651143464" data-published-at="1616167731" id="rebelltitem3">
                       &lt;p&gt;&lt;a target="_blank" href="https://www.penguinrandomhouse.com/books/652791/what-can-i-do-by-jane-fonda/" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;What Can I Do? From Climate Despair to Action&lt;/a&gt;, by Jane Fonda (Penguin Random House 2020, 352 pages, $30.00)&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;In the fall of 2019, frustrated with the obvious inaction of politicians and inspired by Greta Thunberg and student climate strikers, Jane Fonda moved to Washington, D.C., to lead weekly climate change demonstrations on Capitol Hill. On October 11, she launched Fire Drill Fridays, and has since led thousands of people in nonviolent civil disobedience. In What Can I Do?, Fonda weaves her deeply personal journey as an activist with conversations and speeches by leading climate scientists and inspiring community organizers. She dives deep into issues – like water, migration, and human rights – to emphasize what is at stake. More, Fonda equips us with the tools we need to join her in protest, so that everyone can work to combat the climate crisis.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;(Editor's note: 100% of the author's net proceeds from What Can I Do? go to Greenpeace.)&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;&lt;/em&gt;&lt;a target="_blank" href="https://www.rizzoliusa.com/book/9780847869329/"&gt;Who Cares Wins: Reasons for Optimisms in Our Changing World&lt;/a&gt;, by Lily Cole (Rizzoli 2020, 480 pages, $35.00)&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;The climate crisis, mass extinctions, political polarization, extreme inequality – the world faces terrifying challenges that threaten to divide us. Yet activist and filmmaker Lily Cole argues that it is up to us to actively choose optimism, collaborate, make changes, and define what is possible: "We are the ancestors of our future. The choices we make now and the actions we take today will define and transform future generations." Cole explores divisive issues from fast fashion to fast food and from renewable energy to gender equality, and interviews some of today's greatest influencers. The book also features a 32-page photo insert documenting Lily's experiences and vision, as well as the artists, activists, and others who have inspired her.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
                      </div>
                      <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-4" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/climate-change-books-women" data-id="4" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651143464" data-published-at="1616167731" id="rebelltitem4">
                       &lt;p&gt;&lt;a target="_blank" href="https://utorontopress.com/us/the-new-climate-activism-2" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;The New Climate Activism: NGO Authority and Participation in Climate Change Governance&lt;/a&gt;, by Jen Iris Allan (University of Toronto Press 2021, 226 pages, $32.95 paperback)&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;At the 2019 UN climate change conference, activists and delegates from groups representing Indigenous, youth, women, and labor rights were among those marching through the halls chanting "Climate Justice, People Power." In The New Climate Activism, Jen Iris Allan looks at why and how these social activists came to participate in climate change governance while others remain outside of climate activism. As a result, concepts such as gender mainstreaming, just transition, and climate justice are common terms, while human rights and health remain "fringe issues" in climate change governance. The New Climate Activism explores why and how some activists brought their issues to climate change, and succeeded, while others did not.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;&lt;/em&gt;&lt;a target="_blank" href="https://powerhousearena.com/shop/cool-women-leaders-reversing-global-warming"&gt;Cool: Women Leaders Reversing Global Warming&lt;/a&gt;, by Paola Gianturco and Avery Sangster (Powerhouse Books 2021, 192 pages, $39.95)&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Women are especially effective leaders when it comes to combating global warming. Christiana Figueres and Tom Rivett-Carnac, architects of the 2015 Paris Agreement, report that "Nations with greater female representation in positions of power have smaller climate footprints. Companies with women on their executive boards are more likely to invest in renewable energy and develop products that help solve the climate crisis." For this book, Paola Gianturco and her granddaughter and co-author, Avery Sangster, interviewed and photographed women leaders, of organizations public and private, from around the world. COOL tells their inspiring stories in their own words and suggests actions you can take to join them on this existential journey.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
                      </div>
                      <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-5" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/climate-change-books-women" data-id="5" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651143464" data-published-at="1616167731" id="rebelltitem5">
                       &lt;p&gt;&lt;a target="_blank" href="https://www.penguinrandomhouse.com/books/645808/all-we-can-save-by-edited-by-ayana-elizabeth-johnson-and-katharine-k-wilkinson/" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;All We Can Save: Truth, Courage and Solutions for the Climate Crisis&lt;/a&gt;, edited by Ayana Elizabeth Johnson and Katharine K. Wilkinson (Penguin Random House 2020, 448 pages, $29.00)&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;There is a renaissance blooming in the climate movement: leadership that is more characteristically feminine and more faithfully feminist, rooted in compassion, connection, creativity, and collaboration. All We Can Save illuminates the expertise and insights of dozens of diverse women leading on climate in the United States – scientists, journalists, farmers, lawyers, teachers, activists, and designers, across generations, geographies, and race – and aims to advance a more representative and solution-oriented public conversation on the climate crisis. Curated by two climate leaders and intermixing essays with poetry and art, this book is both a balm and a guide, bolstering our resolve never to give up on one another or our collective future.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;&lt;/em&gt;&lt;a target="_blank" href="https://about.bnef.com/blog/more-gender-diversity-on-corporate-boards-makes-for-better-climate-governance-and-innovation/"&gt;Gender Diversity and Climate Innovation&lt;/a&gt;, by (Bloomberg NEF 2020, 39 pages, free download available &lt;a target="_blank" href="https://assets.bbhub.io/professional/sites/24/BNEF-Sasakawa-Peace-Foundation-Gender-Diversity-and-Climate-Innovation_12012020_FINAL.pdf"&gt;here&lt;/a&gt;)&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;A proportion of 30% or more for women on corporate boards has shown a positive correlation with better climate governance and innovation in the global electric utilities, oil and gas, and mining sectors over the last four years, according to a new report by BloombergNEF and Sasakawa Peace Foundation. Gender diversity does not directly contribute to lowering emissions, but integrated oil companies with higher female representation at the board level, for example, are also more likely to have a set of decarbonization strategies and to have invested in digitalization activities. Gender Diversity and Climate Innovation examines the impact of gender diversity on climate governance, climate performance, innovation, and climate innovation.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;(Editor's note: See also the report just released by Sustainable Policy Institute, &lt;a target="_blank" href="https://www.omfif.org/gbi2021/"&gt;Gender Balance Index 2021&lt;/a&gt;.)&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
                      </div>
                      <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-6" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/climate-change-books-women" data-id="6" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651143464" data-published-at="1616167731" id="rebelltitem6">
                       &lt;p&gt;&lt;a target="_blank" href="https://www.penguinrandomhouse.com/books/617060/under-a-white-sky-by-elizabeth-kolbert/" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;Under a White Sky: The Nature of the Future&lt;/a&gt;, by Elizabeth Kolbert (Penguin Random House 2021, 256 pages, $28.00)&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;In Under a White Sky, Elizabeth Kolbert takes a hard look at the new world we are creating. Along the way, she meets biologists who are trying to preserve the world's rarest fish, which lives in a single tiny pool in the middle of the Mojave; engineers who are turning carbon emissions to stone in Iceland; Australian researchers who are trying to develop a "super coral" that can survive on a hotter globe; and physicists who are contemplating shooting tiny diamonds into the stratosphere to cool the earth. One way to look at human civilization, says Kolbert, is as a ten-thousand-year exercise in defying nature. By turns inspiring, terrifying, and darkly comic, Under a White Sky is an utterly original examination of the challenges we face.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;&lt;/em&gt;&lt;a target="_blank" href="https://milkweed.org/book/late-migrations"&gt;Late Migrations: A Natural History of Love and Loss&lt;/a&gt;, by Margaret Renkl (Milkweed Editions 2021, 248 pages, $16.95 paperback)&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;From New York Times opinion writer Margaret Renkl comes an unusual, captivating portrait of a family – and of the cycles of joy and grief that inscribe human lives within the natural world. Growing up in Alabama, Renkl was a devoted reader, an explorer of riverbeds and red-dirt roads, and a fiercely loved daughter. Ringing with rapture and heartache, Renkl's linked essays convey the dignity of bluebirds and rat snakes, monarch butterflies and native bees. Renkl suggests that there is astonishment to be found in common things – in what seems ordinary, in what we all share. Illustrated by Billy Renkl, Late Migrations is an assured and memorable debut. (Editor's note: A companion volume, &lt;a target="_blank" href="https://milkweed.org/book/graceland-at-last"&gt;Graceland at Last&lt;/a&gt;, will be published in September.)&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
                      </div>
                      <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-7" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/climate-change-books-women" data-id="7" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651143464" data-published-at="1616167731" id="rebelltitem7">
                       &lt;p&gt;&lt;a target="_blank" href="https://us.macmillan.com/books/9781250204028" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;Migrations: A Novel&lt;/a&gt;, by Charlotte McConaghy (Flatiron Books 2020, 272 pages, $26.99)&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Franny Stone has always been the kind of woman who is able to love but unable to stay. Leaving behind everything but her research gear, she arrives in Greenland with a singular purpose: to follow the last Arctic terns in the world on what might be their final migration to Antarctica. Franny talks her way onto a fishing boat, and she and the crew set sail, traveling ever further from shore and safety. But as Franny's history begins to unspool, it becomes clear that she is chasing more than just the birds. How much is she willing to risk for one more chance at redemption? Epic and intimate, Charlotte McConaghy's Migrations is an ode to a disappearing world and a breathtaking page-turner about the possibility of hope against all odds.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;(Editor's note: Readers can find YCC's interview with the author, by Amy Brady, &lt;a target="_blank" href="https://yaleclimateconnections.org/2020/08/hope-is-the-thing-with-feathers-migrations/"&gt;here&lt;/a&gt;.)&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;&lt;/em&gt;&lt;a target="_blank" href="https://www.penguinrandomhouse.com/books/673583/high-as-the-waters-rise-by-anja-kampmann/" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;High as the Waters Rise: A Novel&lt;/a&gt;, by Anja Kampmann, translated by Anne Posten (Penguin Random House 2020, 320 pages, $26.00)&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;One night aboard an oil drilling platform in the Atlantic, Waclaw returns to his cabin to find that his bunkmate and companion, Mátyás, has gone missing. A search of the rig confirms his fear that Mátyás has fallen into the sea. Grief–stricken, he embarks on an epic emotional and physical journey that takes him to Morocco, to Mátyás's hometown in Hungary, and finally to the mining town of his childhood in Germany. Waclaw's encounters along the way with other lost and yearning souls bring us closer to his origins. High as the Waters Rise is a stirring exploration of male intimacy, the nature of grief, and the cost of freedom. It's the story of a man who stands at the margins of a society from which he has little profited, even though it depends on his labor.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;(Editor's note: Readers can find YCC's interview with the author, by Amy Brady, &lt;a href="https://yaleclimateconnections.org/2020/10/invisible-lives-in-high-as-the-waters-rise/" target="_blank"&gt;here&lt;/a&gt;.)&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;&lt;em&gt;Also see: &lt;/em&gt;&lt;a href="https://yaleclimateconnections.org/2020/03/15-books-about-women-leading-the-way-on-climate-change/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;15 books about women leading the way on climate change&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
                      </div>
                      &lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Reposted with permission from &lt;a href="https://yaleclimateconnections.org/2021/03/new-and-recent-books-about-women-climate-change-and-the-environment/" target="_blank"&gt;Yale Climate Connections&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

             <div class="widget tag-climate-crisis tag-climate-change tag-environment tag-mining tag-rivers post-section--climate-change" data-category="Climate" elid="2651083582">
              <article class="clearfix page-article sm-mb-1 quality-MD post-2651083582" data-is-frozen="false" elid="2651083582">
               <div class="row px10">
                <div class="col sm-mb-1" id="col-center" style="width:100.0%;">

                      By Andrea Germanos
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      The U.S. Environmental Protection Agency (
                      <a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/epa">
                       EPA
                      </a>
                      ) on Thursday brought back its climate change website — a resource the former Trump administration had yanked.

https://t.co/WuC789TKue https://t.co/IXCrji7Biw&lt;/div&gt; &amp;mdash; Select Committee on the Climate Crisis (@Select Committee on the Climate Crisis)&lt;a href="https://twitter.com/ClimateCrisis/statuses/1372618034335072257"&gt;1616092616.0&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
                      </div>
                      <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-2" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/epa-climate-science-biden-trump" data-id="2" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651142667" data-published-at="1616165212" id="rebelltitem2">
                       &lt;p&gt;"Climate facts are back on EPA's website where they should be," newly confirmed EPA Administrator Michael Regan &lt;a href="https://www.epa.gov/newsreleases/epa-reboots-climate-change-website" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;said&lt;/a&gt; in a statement Thursday.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"Considering the urgency of this crisis, it's critical that Americans have access to information and resources so that we can all play a role in protecting our environment, our health, and vulnerable communities," Regan continued. "Trustworthy, science-based information is at the foundation of strong, achievable solutions."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;New information on climate science and the crisis' impacts will soon be added to the website, the statement added.&lt;/p&gt;
                      </div>
                      <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-3" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/epa-climate-science-biden-trump" data-id="3" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651142667" data-published-at="1616165212" id="rebelltitem3">
                       &lt;p&gt;In April of 2017 the Trump administration, with Scott Pruitt then at the helm of the EPA, &lt;a href="https://thehill.com/policy/energy-environment/331185-epa-removes-climate-change-page-from-website-amid-updates" target="_blank"&gt;rendered&lt;/a&gt; the agency's climate change site basically useless, with readers being redirected to a page that said, "This page is being updated." Any pretense of ongoing or pending updates, however, was &lt;a href="https://www.commondreams.org/news/2018/11/02/deleted-under-trump-epa-websites-climate-section-page-not-found" target="_blank"&gt;dropped&lt;/a&gt; in 2018. The moves were seen as on-brand for an administration carrying out a war on &lt;a href="http://www.ecowatch.com/science/"&gt;science&lt;/a&gt; and pushing forth pro-fossil fuel policies.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The relaunching of the site was welcomed by the Union of Concerned Scientists, who &lt;a href="https://twitter.com/UCSUSA/status/1372608779511066627" target="_blank"&gt;said&lt;/a&gt; it was "back and better than ever!"&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"The EPA is restoring science and reinstating its climate website, making it a priority as @EPAMichaelRegan leads the way in transitioning our nation to a clean energy economy," the group tweeted.&lt;/p&gt;
                      </div>
                      <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-6" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/epa-climate-science-biden-trump" data-id="6" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651142667" data-published-at="1616165212" id="rebelltitem6">
                       &lt;div id="a3b33" class="rm-shortcode" data-rm-shortcode-id="2938e4257f4d5f951e70c5b2c6e6b77e"&gt;&lt;blockquote class="twitter-tweet twitter-custom-tweet" data-twitter-tweet-id="1372624935563231241" data-partner="rebelmouse"&gt;&lt;div style="margin:1em 0"&gt;After 4 years of climate denial, the @EPA is restoring science at the agency! Step one: reinstating its climate web… https://t.co/qvuzVaflKb&lt;/div&gt; &amp;mdash; AFGE Local 704 (@AFGE Local 704)&lt;a href="https://twitter.com/704afge/statuses/1372624935563231241"&gt;1616094261.0&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
                      </div>
                      <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-4" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/epa-climate-science-biden-trump" data-id="4" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651142667" data-published-at="1616165212" id="rebelltitem4">
                       &lt;p&gt;Progressive advocacy group Environment America &lt;a href="https://environmentamerica.org/news/ame/statement-epa-acts-responsibly-relaunching-climate-science-and-policy-website" target="_blank"&gt;said&lt;/a&gt; the "relaunch is a strong signal that the Biden administration will restore the role of science in protecting our communities and public health."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The move was also welcomed by climate action advocate and Washington Gov. Jay Inslee.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"For the first time in 4 years, the @EPA is providing information on climate change through its website. The public now has access to data and science about this existential threat. I am glad to see the federal government back in the fight for our future," Inslee &lt;a href="https://twitter.com/GovInslee/status/1372624976851836929" target="_blank"&gt;tweeted&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
                      </div>
                      <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-5" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/epa-climate-science-biden-trump" data-id="5" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651142667" data-published-at="1616165212" id="rebelltitem5">
                       &lt;p&gt;A similar message was fired off by Regan, who &lt;a href="https://twitter.com/EPAMichaelRegan/status/1372619108374679554" target="_blank"&gt;tweeted&lt;/a&gt;: "Climate change impacts all of us. You deserve access to science and data so we can find solutions together."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Regan, who'd been &lt;a href="https://www.commondreams.org/news/2020/12/17/michael-regan-nc-official-reportedly-tapped-be-bidens-epa-head-urged-genuinely" target="_blank"&gt;serving&lt;/a&gt; as the top environmental official in North Carolina, was confirmed as EPA administrator last week.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Donna Chavis, senior fossil fuel campaigner for Friends of the Earth and an elder of the Lumbee Nation, said at the time that "Regan and the EPA have a new opportunity to place environmental justice at the center of the agency and the United States' approach to the climate crisis."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Chavis also urged Regan to "take bold and visionary steps to rebuild the EPA and address the very real climate crisis we face in the U.S and globally. It is time we all do better."&lt;/p&gt;
                      </div>
                      &lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Reposted with permission from &lt;a href="https://www.commondreams.org/news/2021/03/18/after-four-dark-years-under-trump-words-climate-and-science-are-back-epa-website" target="_blank"&gt;Common Dreams&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;br/&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

                  <h2 class="widget__headline h2">
                   <a aria-label="5 Things to Know About the Fate of Wild Salmon" class="widget__headline-text custom-post-headline" data-type="text" href="https://www.ecowatch.com/wild-salmon-extinction-2651142872.html">
                    5 Things to Know About the Fate of Wild Salmon
                   </a>
                  </h2>
                  <div class="social-author clearfix">
                   <div class="social-author__avatar image">
                    <div class="cover-all image" style='background-image: url("https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy85OTcyNTkwL29yaWdpbi5qcGciLCJleHBpcmVzX2F0IjoxNjU5MTAyNDQ4fQ.Rq8YEmEa3xC-IhAmgub2ebaW0Rqpt66kaHUUd25xfXU/img.jpg?width=210")'>

                    The Revelator

                   <div class="body-description">
                    <div class="widget__brief">
                     <p>
                      By Tara Lohan
                      <br/>
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      It's not too hard to find salmon on a menu in the United States, but that seeming abundance — much of it fueled by overseas fish farms — overshadows a grim reality on the ground. Many of our wild salmon, outside Alaska, are on the ropes — and have been for decades.
                     </p>
                    </div>
                    <div class="content-container">
                    </div>
                    <div class="js-appear-on-expand">
                     <template>
                      <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-1" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/wild-salmon-extinction" data-id="1" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651142872" data-published-at="1616163944" id="rebelltitem1">
                       &lt;p&gt;Twenty years ago Pacific salmon were found to have disappeared from 40% of their native rivers and streams across Oregon, Washington, Idaho and California. In places where they remain, like the Columbia River system, the number of wild fish returning to streams is estimated to &lt;a href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/09/16/science/chinook-salmon-columbia.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;have plunged&lt;/a&gt; by as much as 98%. Today &lt;a href="https://www.fisheries.noaa.gov/species/pacific-salmon-and-steelhead#esa-protected-species" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;28 populations of West Coast salmon and steelhead&lt;/a&gt; are listed as threatened or endangered under the Endangered Species Act.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;New research is helping to put the problem — and solutions — into focus. But in some cases, policy to implement changes still lags.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h2&gt;1. Trouble in Washington&lt;/h2&gt;&lt;p&gt;With 14 salmon and steelhead species listed as endangered in Washington, a &lt;a href="https://stateofsalmon.wa.gov/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/StateofSalmonExecSummary2020.pdf" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;new report&lt;/a&gt; by the state declared that "too many salmon remain on the brink of extinction. And time is running out." Four key factors, the researchers say, have been attributed to their historical decline: habitat, harvest, hydropower and hatcheries.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h2&gt;2. Upstream Changes&lt;/h2&gt;&lt;p&gt;Along with historic threats, there's another new factor making salmon recovery challenging for Washington and other West Coast states: climate change. Increasing temperatures are causing &lt;a href="https://therevelator.org/snow-droughts-west/" target="_blank"&gt;snowpack declines&lt;/a&gt;, resulting in warmer streams that can stress or kill salmon. Additionally, more precipitation falling as rain instead of snow causes rivers to run faster earlier in the season, which can wash away salmon nests and sweep young salmon out of their calm-water habitat before they're ready — reducing their chances of survival.&lt;/p&gt;
                      </div>
                      <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-2" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/wild-salmon-extinction" data-id="2" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651142872" data-published-at="1616163944" id="rebelltitem2">
                       &lt;h2&gt;3. Ocean Woes&lt;/h2&gt;&lt;p&gt;It's not just freshwater habitat for salmon that's changing. A recent study in the journal &lt;em&gt;Communications Biology&lt;/em&gt; looked at how eight populations of wild spring-summer Chinook from the Snake River Basin fared during the ocean phase of their lives. And it's not good. If ocean warming continues, by the 2060s &lt;a href="https://www.nature.com/articles/s42003-021-01734-w" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;mortality for Chinook could be as high as 90%&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h2&gt;4. Ripple Effect&lt;/h2&gt;&lt;p&gt;Pacific salmon are an integral cultural resource for Pacific Northwest tribes and provide thousands of regional jobs. But the fish don't just feed people. They also nourish freshwater and marine ecosystems, along with more than 100 species.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;And for one animal in particular, the critically endangered Southern Resident killer whale (&lt;em&gt;Orcinus orca&lt;/em&gt;), the &lt;a href="https://www.washington.edu/news/2019/12/16/resident-orcas-chinook-salmon/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;decline of Chinook is an existential threat&lt;/a&gt;. It's been long known that Southern Residents feed primarily on Chinook — the largest Pacific salmon species — during the summer. But a new &lt;a href="https://journals.plos.org/plosone/article?id=10.1371/journal.pone.0247031" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;study&lt;/a&gt; published in the journal &lt;em&gt;Plos One&lt;/em&gt; found that Chinook were also important year-round.&lt;/p&gt;
                      </div>
                      <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-3" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/wild-salmon-extinction" data-id="3" data-is-image="True" data-post-id="2651142872" data-published-at="1616163944" id="rebelltitem3">
                       &lt;img lazy-loadable="true" data-runner-src="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTg1MTUyOS9vcmlnaW4uanBnIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTYyNjk5NzE0M30.gbiLMP0sLZO2nk3bNKdrqziwJVqem9_5vR0TqX_S3MQ/img.jpg?width=980" id="3b49d" class="rm-shortcode" data-rm-shortcode-id="66909ed700a486af4a5db5199fed01b8" data-rm-shortcode-name="rebelmouse-image"   data-width="800" data-height="531" /&gt;
                       <small class="image-media media-photo-credit">
                       </small>
                       <p>
                        Southern Resident killer whales. NOAA
                       </p>
                      </div>
                      <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-4" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/wild-salmon-extinction" data-id="4" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651142872" data-published-at="1616163944" id="rebelltitem4">
                       &lt;h2&gt;5. Implementing Solutions&lt;/h2&gt;&lt;p&gt;In an effort to help the recovery of Southern Residents and help boost salmon populations in the region, conservation groups have increased their &lt;a href="https://earthjustice.org/features/long-winding-swim-salmon-snake-river-dams" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;calls to remove four dams&lt;/a&gt; on the Lower Snake River, a major tributary of the Columbia River in Washington.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;While the &lt;a href="https://www.spokesman.com/stories/2021/feb/25/scientists-say-removing-snake-river-dams-is-necess/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;science supports dam removal&lt;/a&gt; to save salmon, putting that into action has run into a wall of political opposition — mostly from conservatives. However, a &lt;a href="https://www.spokesman.com/stories/2021/mar/07/fate-of-republican-mike-simpsons-plan-to-remove-sn/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;recent plan&lt;/a&gt; proposed by Idaho Rep. Mike Simpson to breach the Snake River dams was a rare showing of Republican support, which could signal more bipartisan efforts ahead.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Other dam removals — both &lt;a href="https://therevelator.org/elwha-dam-removal/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;large&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href="https://therevelator.org/cleveland-forest-dam-removal/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;small&lt;/a&gt; — have proved beneficial for salmon in Washington and other states. In California a &lt;a href="https://insideclimatenews.org/news/05012021/floooding-rice-fields-salmon-sacramento-river/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;groundbreaking project&lt;/a&gt; to allow rivers to flood fallow farm fields in winter has helped provide both food and rearing habitat for salmon — and has helped prove that water managers don't have to choose between fish and farmers.&lt;/p&gt;
                      </div>
                      &lt;p&gt;&lt;a href="https://therevelator.org/author/taralohan/" target="_blank"&gt;&lt;em&gt;Tara Lohan &lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;em&gt;is deputy editor of The Revelator and has worked for more than a decade as a digital editor and environmental journalist focused on the intersections of energy, water and climate. Her work has been published by The Nation, American Prospect, High Country News, Grist, Pacific Standard and others. She is the editor of two books on the global water crisis.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Reposted with permission from &lt;a href="https://therevelator.org/pacific-salmon-coverage" target="_blank"&gt;The Revelator&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

                  <h2 class="widget__headline h2">
                   <a aria-label="What Can We Learn From Our Ancestors, the Climate Crisis and Massacres?" class="widget__headline-text custom-post-headline" data-type="text" href="https://www.ecowatch.com/climate-crisis-ancient-massacres-2651138772.html">
                    What Can We Learn From Our Ancestors, the Climate Crisis and Massacres?
                   </a>
                  </h2>
                  <div class="social-author clearfix">
                   <div class="social-author__avatar image">
                    <div class="cover-all image" style='background-image: url("https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yMjg5OTI1OS9vcmlnaW4uanBnIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTY2MDQ4NTE1Nn0.thjDwW3sHb1x_dIp88VkhNiynXx1CYuR73lhhGtbtVU/img.jpg?width=210")'>
                    </div>
                   </div>
                   <a class="social-author__name" data-type="text" href="https://www.ecowatch.com/u/tiffanyduong1">
                    Tiffany Duong
                   </a>
                  </div>
                  <div class="social-date">
                   <span class="social-date__text">
                    19 March
                   </span>
                  </div>
                  <a class="widget__section js-load-brick-on-click" href="https://www.ecowatch.com/climate-change/">
                   Climate
                  </a>
                 </div>

"order": 9}, {"amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "display": true, "new_amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "order": 10}], "adsOrder": [2]}
                   </script>
                   <div class="body-description">
                    <div class="widget__brief">
                     <p>
                      About 6,200 years ago, 41 people were killed and buried in a mass grave in what is now modern-day Croatia. According to
                      <a href="https://www.livescience.com/prehistoric-massacre-croatia.html" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
                       Live Science
                      </a>
                      , DNA analysis has now revealed that members of their own community may have murdered them, and some researchers suggest that a sudden
                      <a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/population-growth" target="_self">
                       population boom
                      </a>
                      or shift in
                      <a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/climate-change/" target="_self">
                       climate conditions
                      </a>
                      could have prompted the mass murder.
                     </p>
                    </div>
                    <div class="content-container">
                    </div>
                    <div class="js-appear-on-expand">
                     <template>
                      <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-1" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/climate-crisis-ancient-massacres" data-id="1" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651138772" data-published-at="1616161427" id="rebelltitem1">
                       &lt;p&gt;The grave was discovered in 2007 in a small village in the hills of Potočani, Croatia. Heavy rains exposed a pit containing dozens of skeletons, Live Science reported. The mass grave was small, about 6.5-feet across and three-feet deep, with at least 41 bodies dumped together.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Archeologists first thought it was a modern grave from World War I or the Croatian War of Independence in the 1990s, but no contemporary objects were found with the bones, according to Live Science. Radiocarbon dating of bones, soil and pottery fragments confirmed a burial date around 4200 B.C.E.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"This makes Potočani one of the first and earliest cases of systematic killing on a large scale in Europe proven by genetic data," said Mario Novak, the &lt;a href="https://journals.plos.org/plosone/article?id=10.1371/journal.pone.0247332" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;study&lt;/a&gt;'s lead author and head of the Laboratory for Evolutionary Anthropology and Bioarchaeology at the Institute for Anthropological Research in Zagreb, Croatia.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Further inspection of the bones and DNA data revealed "random killing without any concern for age or sex," Novak told Live Science. Men, women and children were killed in relatively equal numbers. Many of the killing blows were strikes to the skull from behind, and there were no indications that the victims tried to defend themselves.&lt;/p&gt;
                      </div>
                      <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-2" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/climate-crisis-ancient-massacres" data-id="2" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651138772" data-published-at="1616161427" id="rebelltitem2">
                       &lt;p&gt;Genetic analysis also revealed that the victims were not a targeted family group, because 70 percent of the deceased were not closely related, Novak explained. But, because the victims' shared homogenic genetic ancestry that was almost identical to other contemporary populations from the region, Novak and his team were able to eliminate the hypothesis that the massacre was related to the arrival of new immigrants. Rather, they believe that the victims were a smaller part of the local, stable population.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;These factors led the researchers to suspect a massacre.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"Basically, [all this] means that the perpetrators did not target a certain age or sex category within this community or even a certain family, as we could see in some similar prehistoric examples from continental Europe," Novak said. "The indiscriminate killing recorded in Potočani shows that this was a pre-planned act, most probably with a goal to completely exterminate this community without any consideration or remorse for their victims."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The Potočani mass grave is similar to others found in modern-day Germany and Austria dating to around 5000 B.C.E., Novak said. In total, scientists have found five or six similar cases from continental Europe so far.&lt;/p&gt;
                      </div>
                      <div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-3" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/climate-crisis-ancient-massacres" data-id="3" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651138772" data-published-at="1616161427" id="rebelltitem3">
                       &lt;p&gt;According to Live Science, the "most likely explanation" for the Potočani killings and the older ones in Germany and Austria are prolonged climate changes in Central Europe that caused &lt;a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/flooding" target="_self"&gt;floods&lt;/a&gt; or &lt;a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/drought" target="_self"&gt;droughts&lt;/a&gt;. These, along with unexpected population booms, possibly led to &lt;a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/food-security" target="_self"&gt;food shortages&lt;/a&gt; and violent competition for resources.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Novak's study called the reasons behind the upsurge of extreme mass violence and massacres during these eras "complex and multifactoral," and agreed that climate-induced drops in agricultural production most likely played a part.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"Human nature hasn't changed much (if at all) since those times," he told EcoWatch. "By studying such ancient massacres, we might try to get a glimpse into the psychology of these people, and maybe try to prevent similar events today," Novak told Live Science.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Novak also said it was obvious that the climate crisis profoundly impacted our distant ancestors as much as today's modern world. He warned, "If we cannot change ourselves and our attitude toward the environment drastically, I'm afraid soon the things will start resembling these ancient massacres, but on a more global scale."&lt;/p&gt;
                      </div>

        function replaceHoursText() {
    var date = document.querySelectorAll('.post-date, .social-date__text');
    date = Object.values(date);
    for(var i=0; i<date.length; i++){
      var str = date[i].innerText;
      var dateElement = date[i];
      var oldFormat = str.split(" ");
      
      if (str.includes("ago")){
      	continue;
      }
      
      if(str.length > 3 && isNaN(oldFormat[0])){
      	continue;
      }
      
      if (str.length > 3){
        //dealing with months
        var newFormat;
        
        if(oldFormat.length==2){
        	newFormat = oldFormat[1].substring(0, 3) + " " + oldFormat[0];
        } else {
            newFormat = oldFormat[1] + " " + oldFormat[0] + ", "+ oldFormat[2]
        } 
        dateElement.innerText = newFormat;
      } else if (str == "1h") {
         dateElement.innerText = str.replace('h', ' hour ago');
      } else if (str.includes("h")) {
         dateElement.innerText = str.replace('h', ' hours ago');
      } else {
         dateElement.innerText = str.replace('m', ' minutes ago');
      }
    }
}

 replaceHoursText();
document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', function() {
    replaceHoursText();
});

setInterval(replaceHoursText, 3000);
    

});
